1401 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



City of Bellevue v. Benyaminov


No. 59243-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


144 Wn. App. 755; 183 P.3d 1127; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1239



May 27, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Bellevue v. Benyaminov, 165 Wn.2d 1020, 203 P.3d 378, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 112 (Wash., Feb. 3, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 06-1-04527-7.SEA. Date filed in Superior Court: 11/3/06. Superior Court Judge Signing: Douglass A. North.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Approximately eight years after his conviction, defendant moved to withdraw his guilty plea to third degree theft. The Superior Court of King County (Washington) reversed the district court's decision denying defendant's motion. The City's motion for discretionary review was granted.


OVERVIEW: The superior court committed legal error by applying equitable tolling to the case, thereby allowing defendant to collaterally attack his conviction, as there was no evidence in defendant's declaration supporting his motion to vacate that evidenced bad faith, deception, or false assurances by the City or anyone else. The record was devoid of any evidence that would have supported equitable tolling of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.93.070 beyond its one-year limit. Moreover, the absence of a written acknowledgement that defendant was advised in accordance with Wash. Rev. Code § 10.40.200(2) did not support equitable tolling of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.93.090's one-year bar as the destruction of court files pursuant to a records retention policy did not prove that no acknowledgement ever existed, nor did an absence of the acknowledgement evidence bad faith, deception, or false assurances by anyone. Finally, the judgment of conviction was not invalid on its face as defendant failed to present the original judgment or a copy of it.


OUTCOME: The superior court's decision was reversed. The district court's decision denying defendant's motion to withdraw the guilty plea as untimely was reinstated.

 

1402 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Stubbs


No. 25475-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


144 Wn. App. 644; 184 P.3d 660; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1202



May 20, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Stubbs, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1494 (Wash. Ct. App., June 20, 2008)
Review pending at State v. Stubbs, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 144 (Wash., Feb. 3, 2009)
Review granted by, in part State v. Stubbs, 165 Wn.2d 1035, 203 P.3d 380, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 223 (2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Stubbs, 170 Wn.2d 117, 240 P.3d 143, 2010 Wash. LEXIS 869 (Wash., Oct. 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT. PEND OREILLE COUNTY. Superior Court No: 05-1-00071-9. Date filed in Superior Court: 9/7/06. Superior Court Judge signing: REBECCA M. BAKER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Superior Court of Pend Oreille County (Washington) of first degree assault while armed with a deadly weapon. The jury also found that the victim's injuries substantially exceeded the level of bodily harm necessary to satisfy the elements of the crime, allowing an exceptional sentence under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(y). Defendant was sentenced to 480 months. Defendant appealed the sentence.


OVERVIEW: During an argument, defendant stabbed the victim in the back of his neck with a knife, causing severe paralysis. The victim dropped a burner he was holding, starting a fire. Defendant ignored the victim's pleas for help and left, so the victim put the fire out with his bare arms while the knife was lodged in his neck. The victim's spinal cord was cut in two, causing paralysis below the waist, including his bladder and intestines, and partial paralysis above the waist and confining the victim to a wheelchair. A doctor predicted an increased risk of pneumonia, stroke, seizure, and death and gave the victim a 17-year shortened life expectancy. Defendant argued that the victim's injuries inhered in first degree assault and could not justify an exceptional sentence. The court disagreed, finding that these severe injuries and ongoing problems were sufficiently severe and did not inhere in the assault. The court rejected defendant's contention that § 9.94A.535(3)(y) was vague because the doctrine did not apply to sentencing schemes and because the statute apprised individuals that inflicting serious bodily injury upon another would subject them to a higher sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's exceptional sentence was affirmed.

 

1403 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Det. of Pouncy


No. 59034-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


144 Wn. App. 609; 184 P.3d 651; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1179



May 19, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by In re Det. of Pouncy, 165 Wn.2d 1007, 198 P.3d 512, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1114 (2008)
Affirmed by, Remanded by In re Det. of Curtis N. Pouncy, 2010 Wash. LEXIS 248 (Wash., Mar. 11, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 03-2-20900-7 SEA. Date filed in Superior Court: October 16, 2006. Superior Court Judge Signing: Hon. Helen Halpert.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a committed individual (appellant), sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which authorized his commitment as a sexually violent predator (SVP) pursuant to the Sexually Violent Predator Act (Act), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 71.09.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of an order authorizing his commitment under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.020(16) as an SVP pursuant to the Act. He argued, in part, that the trial court erred by allowing appellant's expert witness to be impeached through the use of findings of fact entered in an unrelated superior court matter. The appellate court agreed, reversing the judgment. Viewed in context, it was apparent that the State was seeking to introduce findings of fact on an unrelated case on the question of whether the expert witness had acted consistent with the standards of his profession in interviewing and evaluating appellant. That was a matter for expert testimony, not lay testimony. It was apparent that appellant's counsel's objection to the questioning, based on a lack of foundation, was premised upon the State's failure to qualify the prior judge in that unrelated matter as an expert witness in the areas of sex offender evaluation and psychology. That objection was properly made. The prior court's factual findings were not relevant and appellant's objection based on lack of foundation was also correctly interposed and should have been sustained.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment.

 

1404 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Bahr


No. 35315-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1052



May 6, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Marriage of Bahr, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1135 (Wash. Ct. App., May 6, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband (husband) sought review of the decision of the trial court (Washington), which found in favor of respondent ex-wife (wife) and denied the husband's motion to modify or vacate a permanent restraining order in effect since the parties' dissolution of marriage.


OVERVIEW: The husband appealed the trial court's denial of his motion to modify or vacate a permanent restraining order in effect since the dissolution of his marriage. He argued that the order's requirement that he stay 500 feet away from the wife too broadly infringed on his constitutional rights of freedom of travel and movement. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that the record showed that the husband needed to travel a mere 0.2 miles further from his professed regular routes of travel to stay beyond 500 feet from the wife's home and business. Such minimal distances did not reasonably impose an unconstitutional burden on his freedom of travel. The husband was free to move about as he pleased and the restraining order only burdened his freedom of movement by occasionally requiring him to leave a public establishment in the area when the wife happened to be in the same location. Even assuming that his rights to movement and travel were actually implicated, the State was permitted to curtail those rights to protect the wife from any invasive, oppressive, and harmful behavior on the part of the husband.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the wife was awarded fees and costs on appeal.

 

1405 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


City of Cheney v. Bogle


No. 26000-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 999



May 1, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at City of Cheney v. Bogle, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1101 (Wash. Ct. App., May 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 06-2-03218-1. Judge signing: JEROME J. LEVEQUE. Date filed: February 23, 2007.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged a judgment of the Spokane County Superior Court (Washington) granting appellee city partial summary judgment, quieting title to the disputed property to the city, and entering an order and warrant of abatement compelling the landowner to demolish and remove all portions of his building constructed on the right-of-way.


OVERVIEW: The landowner operated an auto repair business from his property, which fronted a street; his building was located at the edge of the city's sidewalk. The city filed an action to quiet title to the 12-foot strip of property condemned by an ordinance in 1889 and to abate the public nuisance created by the encroachment of the building on the public right-of-way. On appeal of the trial court's judgment for the city, the court held that the city presented evidence that it had compensated the owners of the affected land lots by adopting Cheney, Wash., Ordinance No. 83, providing that the city vacated 12 feet of the alley at the rear of the lots. In addition, any challenge to the compensation provided in the ordinance should have been made within 20 days from the time of the award in 1889. The landowner failed to produce any deed in his chain of title conveying the disputed part of the property to him. The court rejected the landowner's equal protection claim because the record reflected nothing that could be construed to imply a deliberate discriminatory purpose on the part of the city. The court also rejected the landowner's equitable estoppel, laches, and waiver claims.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1406 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Segaline v. Dep't of Labor & Indus.


No. 35823-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


144 Wn. App. 312; 182 P.3d 480; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1065



April 29, 2008, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals July 1, 2008.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended by, Reconsideration denied by Segaline v. State, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1584 (Wash. Ct. App., July 1, 2008)
Review pending at Segaline v. Dep't of Labor & Indus., 2009 Wash. LEXIS 335 (Wash., Mar. 3, 2009)
Review granted by Segaline v. Dep't of Labor & Indus., 165 Wn.2d 1044, 205 P.3d 132, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 405 (2009)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Segaline v. Dep't of Labor & Indus., 169 Wn.2d 467, 238 P.3d 1107, 2010 Wash. LEXIS 704 (2010)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] We affirm.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electrical contractor sued respondent state agency for negligent infliction of emotional distress, intentional infliction of emotional distress, malicious prosecution, negligent supervision, and (under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983) violation of his civil rights. A Washington trial court summarily dismissed all claims and awarded the agency statutory damages under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.24.510. The contractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The suit involved the contractor's arrest after a 911 call by agency employees who feared that the contractor would assault them. The court held that the agency was immune from civil liability under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.24.510 because (1) state agencies were "persons" under § 4.24.510; (2) there was no evidence that the agency's communication to police was not in good faith; (3) § 4.24.510 applied to the malicious prosecution claim; and (4) the negligent supervision claim was based upon, or was the result of, the agency's communications to the police. The agency was entitled to attorney fees and costs because it prevailed in its § 4.24.510 defense and there was no evidence of bad faith. Summary judgment on the claim for negligent infliction of emotional distress was proper because any such distress was not reasonably foreseeable. Summary dismissal of the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action was proper because the state was immune from suits under § 1983 for acts of its agents. Finally, the contractor's amended § 1983 claim against an agency employee was untimely because under Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 15(c), the claim related back only to a date over three years after it accrued.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1407 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Hannum v. Dep't of Licensing


No. 36349-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


144 Wn. App. 354; 181 P.3d 915; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1075



April 29, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISHED IN PART


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a husband and wife, filed negligence and negligent infliction of emotional distress claims against respondents, the Washington State Department of Licensing, its director, and employees of the Department. The trial court erred in dismissing their negligence claims under the public duty doctrine and granted summary judgment in favor of the Department. The husband and wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband wrote the Department, asking it to investigate a medical notation in his file. The Department found no documents supporting the medical certificate requirement and removed the notation the next day. The husband obtained his commercial driver's license a few days later. But, by that time, he was no longer enrolled in the school bus driver course. The husband alleged that the instructor told him to leave and not come back when he informed the instructor of the notation. The husband and his wife sued the Department. Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.041 evidenced the legislature's intent to protect the public by ensuring that the Department did not issue licenses to persons who might not be able to safely operate a motor vehicle. The provision allowing a person to prove that despite a mental disability or disease, he or she was capable of driving safely, was simply part of the screening process and did not show a legislative intent to protect a particular class of citizens. Thus, Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.041 did not express a clear intent to protect a particular and circumscribed class of persons. Therefore, the public duty doctrine barred the husband and wife's negligence claims.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1408 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Det. of D.F.F.


No. 59462-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


144 Wn. App. 214; 183 P.3d 302; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 939



April 28, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by In re Det. of D.F.F., 164 Wn.2d 1034, 197 P.3d 1185, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1198 (2008)
Affirmed by, Remanded by In re Det. of D.F.F., 2011 Wash. LEXIS 518 (Wash., July 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: Whatcom Superior Court. Cause No: 06-6-00179-7. Date filed in Superior Court: 1/10/07. Superior Court Judge Signing: Ira Uhrig.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Whatcom County Superior Court (Washington) ordered defendant juvenile involuntarily committed for 90 days of psychiatric treatment following a jury trial. Adhering to the dictate of Wash. Super. Ct. Mental Proc. R. 1.3, the trial court ordered that the entirety of the proceeding be closed to the public. Defendant appealed, challenging the closing of the proceeding and the constitutionality of Rule 1.3.


OVERVIEW: Adhering to the dictate of Rule 1.3, the trial court ordered that the entirety of defendant's commitment proceeding be closed to the public. On appeal, the court first rejected the State's mootness argument; the trial court's order created sufficient adverse consequences such that mootness was not a bar to defendant's appeal. In analyzing Rule 1.3, the court noted that the supreme court had repeatedly articulated an exacting test that trial courts had to apply to determine whether court closure satisfied Wash. Const. art. I, § 10's open justice requirements. A statute or rule was unconstitutional on its face if there were no circumstances where it could constitutionally be applied. Wash. Super. Ct. Mental Proc. R. 1.3 did not allow for any circumstances in which trial judges could perform the analysis required by the supreme court. Thus, Rule 1.3 was unconstitutional on its face. The remedy for holding a statute facially unconstitutional was to render the statute totally inoperative. Because the trial court failed to weigh the relevant competing interests in closing a court proceeding--whether the reason--the remedy was reversal and remand for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's commitment order and remanded the matter for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

1409 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Waterman


No. 59418-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 949



April 28, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Waterman, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 1019 (Wash. Ct. App., Apr. 28, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the trial court (Washington), which convicted him of two counts of attempted first-degree kidnapping and one count of first-degree burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his judgment and sentence for two counts of attempted first-degree kidnapping and one count of first-degree burglary. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that a jury instruction clearly and accurately conveyed that the jury must unanimously agree that one act of assault was proved beyond a reasonable doubt and that the jury must unanimously agree on which act had been proved. Further, the jury's acquittal on the attempted murder counts did not alter the fact that the record contained evidence sufficient to support a conviction based on all alternative means. Unanimity as to guilt, which defendant received, was all that was required. The prosecutor's comments fairly argued the evidence in the record and the credibility of defendant as a witness. Moreover, the prosecutor also reminded jurors to make decisions on the evidence and not on their feelings about the case or on their passions or predispositions. Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.28.020 was not unconstitutionally vague because the phrase "substantial step" clearly advised the public that mere preparation to commit a crime was not a criminal offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1410 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Lawson v. City of Pasco


25967-6-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


144 Wn. App. 203; 181 P.3d 896; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 933



April 24, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Lawson v. City of Pasco, 165 Wn.2d 1012, 199 P.3d 410, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 67 (2009)
Affirmed by Lawson v. City of Pasco, 2010 Wash. LEXIS 342 (Wash., Apr. 15, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT FRANKLIN COUNTY. Superior Court No: 06-2-50398-1. Date filed in Superior Court: 2/23/07. Superior Court Judge signing: CAMERON MITCHELL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Franklin County (Washington) entered an order reversing the determination of appellant city's code enforcement board that respondent owner of a mobile home park violated a valid city ordinance by allowing placement of recreational vehicles in his residential mobile home park. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: Reading Wash. Rev. Code §§ 59.20.040,.080 and.130 together, the legislature expressly conferred concurrent jurisdiction to local municipalities in the field of regulating landlord-tenant compliance with ordinances. Thus, the Manufactured/Mobile Home Landlord-Tenant Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 59.20, did not preempt Pasco, Wash., Mun. Code § 25.40.060. In addition, the Act did not require a landlord to rent a mobile home park lot for placement of a recreational vehicle (park model) in any (or every) particular place within the State. Also, the ordinance in no way attempted to restrict or contradict the provisions of the Act, which expressly deferred to municipal authority in Wash. Rev. Code § 59.20.130(1). Thus, the appellate court concluded that there was no irreconcilable conflict between the Act and the ordinance. Furthermore, the statute and the ordinance could each operate distinctly without inconsistency. Thus, the owner of the mobile home park failed to show that the ordinance was preempted by the Act and was therefore unconstitutional. Accordingly, the ordinance was a valid exercise of municipal police power.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the superior court's order.

 

1411 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Selfridge


No. 36173-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 786



April 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Selfridge, 143 Wn. App. 1055, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 828 (Wash. Ct. App., Apr. 8, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from a trial court (Washington), which convicted him of tampering with witness, contrary to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.72.120(1), and violating a no-contact order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's former wife obtained a no-contact order that prohibited defendant from having contact with her and coming within 500 feet of her residence, school, or workplace. Defendant was later convicted of tampering with a witness and violating the no-contact order. On appeal, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for tampering with a witness. Defendant told a social worker on several occasions that he intended to get his former wife to take back her story regarding his abuse of one of their children. Defendant's subsequent behavior involved reporting unfounded complaints against the former wife for abusing animals and children. Defendant placed a van with derogatory remarks about the former wife in her neighborhood for all to see. However, the State conceded that insufficient evidence supported defendant's conviction for violation of the no-contact order. There was no testimony in the record that the wife was present when defendant came within 500 feet of her residence. Finally, the State properly charged one crime, witness tampering, with a series of acts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the witness tampering conviction. The court vacated defendant's conviction for violation of the no-contact order. The court remanded the case for resentencing.

 

1412 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



LeMond v. Dep't of Licensing


No. 59515-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


143 Wn. App. 797; 180 P.3d 829; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 775



April 7, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 06-2-15807-5 SEA. Date filed in Superior Court: December 1, 2006. Superior Court Judge Signing: Douglass A. North.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Washington Department of Licensing (DOL), appealed from an order of the Superior Court, King County (Washington), that vacated a DOL order suspending the driving privileges of respondent driver. The superior court's order was premised on its conclusion that the doctrine of collateral estoppel applied in the DOL hearing and precluded the DOL from offering evidence in that proceeding of the driver's breath alcohol content.


OVERVIEW: The municipal court entered an order suppressing the blood alcohol content (BAC) test results in the criminal action, but the hearing officer for the DOL admitted the BAC evidence, refusing to apply collateral estoppel. At the administrative hearing, it was incumbent upon the driver to establish not merely that the BAC test results had been excluded in the municipal court proceeding, but also to prove by competent evidence that the issue presented in the license suspension proceeding was identical in all respects to the issue decided in the criminal proceeding, including the applicable legal rules. No transcript of the municipal court proceeding was provided to the appellate court. The municipal court order itself provided no delineation of the basis for its determination. Thus, because the driver failed to present any competent evidence in the DOL hearing tending to prove the precise issues that were decided in the prior municipal court action and the precise legal bases for the municipal court's ruling, collateral estoppel could not properly be applied as to any of the issues presented in the subsequent administrative hearing.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the superior court's judgment.

 

1413 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Welfare of M.R.H.


No. 25703-7-III (consolidated with No. 25704-5-III, No. 25705-3-III, No. 25706-1-III)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


145 Wn. App. 10; 188 P.3d 510; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 695



March 25, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: Order Granting Motion to Publish June 17, 2008.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Welfare of M.R.H., 143 Wn. App. 1045, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 723 (2008)
Review denied by In re Welfare of Hurd, 165 Wn.2d 1009, 198 P.3d 512, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1074 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hurd v. Washington, 556 U.S. 1158, 129 S. Ct. 1682, 173 L. Ed. 2d 1046, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 2452 (U.S., Mar. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 05-7-00224-2 (NOS. 25703-7-III & 25706-1-III), 05-7-00225-1 (NOS. 25704-5-III & 25705-3-III). Judge signing: CARRIE L. RUNGE. Date filed: October 27, 2006.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents appealed the judgment of the Benton County Superior Court (Washington) that terminated their parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The father argued, inter alia, that the Washington Department of Social and Health Services failed to provide all services reasonably necessary to correct his parental deficiencies. The court of appeals disagreed. The testimony at trial established that the department offered the father services both prior to and after his incarceration, but that he did not feel that he was in need of such services. According to the record, the father met with the children's guardian ad litem prior to his incarceration to discuss what services he needed to accomplish. The father made no attempt or was unwilling to participate in services once he was released from prison. The father admitted at trial that he was physically violent during his relationship with the mother, but he did not go to the court ordered anger management classes because he had previously attended such a class and did not think he was in need of that service. He also said he was aware parenting classes were being recommended to him during the course of the proceedings, but he did not feel he had to engage in those services because he had previously completed such a class.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1414 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Pers. Restraint of Albritton


No. 58832-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


143 Wn. App. 584; 180 P.3d 790; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 689



March 24, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause Nos: 03-1-06627-0.SEA; 05-1-08411-8.SEA; 05-1-13596-1.SEA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The King County Superior Court (Washington) sentenced petitioner inmate under the Washington Drug Offender Sentencing Alternative (DOSA). After the inmate violated the community custody conditions of his DOSA sentence, he was reincarcerated. The Washington Department of Corrections (DOC) then recalculated his sentence. The inmate filed a personal restraint petition challenging the DOC's calculation.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was not entitled to receive credit for the periods of time when he was either absent from supervision or was incarcerated on unrelated charges. But, under the DOSA statute, former Wash. Rev. Stat. § 9.94A.660, the appellate court found that the inmate was entitled to credit for the time spent in confinement for violating the community custody conditions of that sentence. The appellate court also determined that, absent evidence to the contrary, the presumption would be that tolling of his community custody under former Wash. Rev. Stat. § 9.94A.625 began on the date the inmate failed to report to his community corrections officer (CCO), not the date of the inmate's last contact with his CCO. Finally, if the DOC terminated the inmate from the DOSA program and revoked the DOSA sentence, the alternative DOSA sentence became a sentence like any other and the inmate was then subject to all rules relating to earned release time in the same way as other inmates. Thus, when the inmate was terminated from the DOSA program and reincarcerated to serve his full sentence, he was entitled to credit for the time he served in jail for violating the conditions of his 2004 DOSA sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted the inmate's personal restraint petition in part and remanded the case to the DOC to recalculate the inmate's release date.

 

1415 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Terhorst


No. 35479-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 649



March 18, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Terhorst, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 711 (Wash. Ct. App., Mar. 18, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court convicted defendant of possession of methamphetamine, possession of less than 40 grams of marijuana, use of drug paraphernalia, and third degree driving with a suspended or revoked license. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury that they must unanimously agree about which act constituted the drug paraphernalia charge. The appellate court found that the unanimity rule did not apply because the case involved a continuing course of conduct. There was no basis for the jury to find unwitting possession as to some items and not others. Had defense counsel requested the unanimity instruction, the jury's verdict would have been the same. The prohibition against the possession and consumption of controlled substances under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.700(4)(c) was too broad. The alcohol prohibition was too broad and had to be modified to preclude only the consumption of alcohol. The prohibition of possession of deadly weapons was not related to defendant's crime. There was no claim that defendant had been charged with violating the condition requiring law abiding behavior. Defendant's claim that the State violated her right to a speedy trial was without merit. The charge itself referred to the correct statute and included all of the elements of the crime. Defendant's argument about trial counsel could not be reviewed on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the convictions, but remanded for modification of the sentence.

 

1416 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Storedahl Props., LLC v. Clark County


No. 35608-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


143 Wn. App. 489; 178 P.3d 377; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 591



March 11, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Storedahl Props., LLC v. Clark County, 164 Wn.2d 1018, 195 P.3d 88, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 860 (Wash., Sept. 4, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mine operator sued respondent county, seeking a declaratory judgment that the county's clean water charge (CWC) was an invalid property tax and not a regulatory fee imposed under Wash. Const. art. XI, §11. A Washington trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the county. The mine operator appealed.


OVERVIEW: Washington courts applied three factors to decide whether a charge was a regulatory fee or a tax: (1) whether the primary purpose was to raise revenue (tax) or to regulate (regulatory fee); (2) whether the money collected had to be allocated only to the authorized regulatory purpose; and (3) whether there was a direct relationship between the fee charged and: (a) the service received by those who paid the fee, or (b) the burden produced by the fee payer. Applying these factors, the court noted that: (1) the CWC was limited to purposes such as paying the cost and expense of regulating, monitoring and evaluating storm water impacts and maintaining and operating storm water control facilities; (2) the county deposited CWC service charges, interest, and penalties for delinquent payments and earnings thereon in a special fund that could be used only for the CWC's purposes; (3) the CWC provided a service to its payers by providing storm water facilities to accommodate their storm water runoff; and (4) the CWC alleviated the burdens that its payers created by working to clean up water pollution and to offset the detrimental impacts of storm water running off impervious surfaces.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1417 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Steward


No. 35739-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 602



March 11, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Steward, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 657 (Wash. Ct. App., Mar. 11, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court convicted defendant of first degree kidnapping and second degree assault convictions with deadly weapon enhancements. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the absence of first degree assault was an element of second degree assault; therefore, the State failed to allege this element in the information, in the jury instructions, and the State failed to prove this element at trial. The appellate court noted that the absence of first degree assault was not an essential element of second degree assault and because the State did not charge defendant with first degree assault, the information language charging defendant with only second degree assault was sufficient. Because the absence of first degree assault was not an element of second degree assault and the State did not charge defendant with first degree assault, the jury to-convict instruction for second degree assault was not deficient. The legislative and judicial branches of the state government did not violate the separation of powers doctrine in using common law to define "assault." Defendant failed to show that the trial court's knowledge instruction was error. The evidence supported the mental-state element of defendant's first degree kidnapping conviction. The record showed that trial counsel discussed the case and the State's evidence with defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1418 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brooks


No. 59069-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 573



March 10, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Brooks, 143 Wn. App. 1029, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 610 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 26.50.110(1) and (5), a Washington trial court convicted and sentenced defendant for felony violation of a no contact order. Defendant challenged the judgment of conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant conceded that one prior conviction was issued under the statutes enumerated in Wash. Rev. Code § 26.50.110(5), but argued that there was insufficient evidence of a second predicate offense. One exhibit showed a misdemeanor charge for violating former Wash. Rev. Code § 26.50.110, which proved that defendant violated a protection order issued under Wash. Rev. Code ch 26.50. A second exhibit showed that he had a misdemeanor conviction for violating former Wash. Rev. Code § 10.99.040, which was a conviction for violating a no contact order issued under a statute enumerated in Wash. Rev. Code § 26.50.110(5). Thus, either exhibit proved the second predicate conviction. The pleas entered in the two prior cases were constitutionally valid where the plea form that defendant signed and the judge accepted informed him of his right to call witnesses, which included the right to testify himself. The information was sufficient as it was not required to include that defendant's threat was a true threat. Finally, the doctrine of invited error barred defendant from claiming a jury instruction error as his proposed jury instructions had been given.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1419 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Murray


No. 59039-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 575



March 10, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Murray, 143 Wn. App. 1029, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 608 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Washington) convicted defendant of felony violation of a court order. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant asserted that his guilty plea in one of his predicate convictions was constitutionally deficient, and argued that the trial court abused its discretion in amending the jury instructions before the jury's deliberations. The appellate court disagreed, finding that defendant's statements clearly evinced his knowing, intelligent, and voluntary waiver of his right to testify. By signing the forms, he stated that he understood that he was waiving several enumerated rights, including the right to confront witnesses and the right to remain silent. The advice of rights instructed defendant that he could choose to waive his right to remain silent and be questioned as any other witness. This was sufficient to advise him of his right to testify. As such, the State demonstrated the constitutional validity of the challenged conviction. Further, the trial court properly corrected an error before the jury began deliberating in order to reflect the terminology that both parties had agreed upon before the jury was originally instructed. There was no allegation that the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions based on the law submitted to the jury in final form.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1420 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Madsen


No. 58662-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 578



March 10, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Madsen, 143 Wn. App. 1028, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 605 (2008)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Washington) convicted defendant of three counts of felony violation of a no-contact order involving three telephone calls to his former girlfriend. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in repeatedly denying his timely, unequivocal requests to proceed pro se, and the sentencing court erred in finding that the telephone calls did not encompass the same criminal conduct. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the trial court initially continued the hearings and deferred its rulings pending appointment of new counsel and concerns over defendant's competency. After both deferred rulings, defendant allowed new counsel to represent him for substantial periods of time before changing his mind and reasserting his request to proceed pro se; and his persistent disruptions impaired the orderly administration of justice. As such, defendant was not entitled to claim that the timeliness of his motion should have been measured from the date of his first request. The sentencing court did not abuse its discretion in finding that defendant did not meet the "same intent" prong of the same criminal conduct test because over eight minutes elapsed between the first and second calls, and over 15 minutes between the second and third calls, and each call was clearly terminated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

1421 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Nelson Alaska Seafoods, Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue


No. 35396-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


143 Wn. App. 455; 177 P.3d 1161; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 499



March 4, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Nelson Alaska Seafoods, Inc. v. Dep't of Dep't of, 164 Wn.2d 1018, 195 P.3d 89, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 880 (Wash., Sept. 4, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation engaged in the harvest, purchase, and resale of geoducks. Subsequently, it filed for a refund of the enhanced food fish taxes it paid. Appellee, the Washington Department of Revenue (Department), denied the corporation's refund request. An administrative law judge denied the corporation's appeal. It then appealed to the Washington trial court, which granted the Department's summary judgment motion. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Washington Department of Natural Resources (DNR) auctioned the right to commercially harvest geoducks on specified tracts of state owned land. After the bidding process, the DNR and the successful bidder entered into a contract that specified a contract price per pound for harvesting geoducks. The corporation paid approximately $ 85,853.86 for the enhanced food fish tax. The corporation argued that the legislature did not intend, under former Wash. Rev. Code § 82.27.020(1), to tax the harvester of geoducks purchased from the DNR. However, the taxing statute, both before and after the 1985 amendment, required an excise tax on the commercial possession of enhanced food fish. Also, the plain language of Wash. Rev. Code § 82.27.020(1) supported the imposition of the enhanced food fish tax on the corporation because it was the first commercial owner of the geoducks. In addition, the tax did not apply to the DNR because it only regulated commercial geoduck harvesting and did not engage in the commercial possession of the geoducks. Thus, the corporation's request for a refund on the enhanced food fish taxes it paid was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1422 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


In re Detention of Johnson


No. 57240-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 470



March 3, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Det. of Johnson, 143 Wn. App. 1022, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 548 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In early 2005, petitioner, who was confined as a sexually violent predator (SVP), sought an unconditional release trial pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.090(2)(c)(ii)(A). The Snohomish County Superior Court, Washington, struck petitioner's trial date based on amendments to Washington's SVP statute. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 2004, the court decided In re Detention of Young in which an SVP offered expert opinion at his order to show cause hearing that his advanced age meant he was no longer likely to commit acts of predatory sexual violence and thus did not continue to meet the definition of an SVP. The expert opinion was based on actuarial risk assessment. The Young court held the evidence presented sufficient to show probable cause warranting a new commitment trial. In 2005, the legislature amended Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.090 finding the decision in Young to be contrary to the legislature's intent and established that a mere change in a demographic factor alone, such as age, was insufficient to establish probable cause warranting a new commitment trial. The court concluded that petitioner was entitled to a full evidentiary hearing. The triggering event for application of the 2005 amendments to the SVP statute was the initial probable cause hearing. Since petitioner's probable cause hearing occurred before the amendments to § 71.09.090 came into effect in May 2005, their application to petitioner was improperly retroactive.


OUTCOME: The order striking petitioner's trial date was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

1423 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Perez


No. 35379-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 459



February 26, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Perez, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 523 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 26, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a Washington trial court, defendant was convicted of methamphetamine manufacture. Defendant appealed, arguing that the search that revealed a "rolling methamphetamine lab" in the trunk of the car he was driving was unlawful.


OVERVIEW: The State conceded that an initial warrantless search of the trunk was unlawful, but argued that the affidavit supporting a subsequent search, absent the improperly obtained information, was sufficient to establish probable cause to search the trunk. The challenged evidence was seized not during the initial search, but during the subsequent search. The trial court had made no findings as to whether police officers would have sought a warrant for the trunk if they had not illegally seen the trunk's contents. Accordingly, the appellate court held that remand was necessary for the trial court to resolve this factual issue. If the trial court were to find that the officers would have sought a warrant, the next issue would be whether an issuing magistrate could have found probable cause to issue the warrant based on the officers' affidavit with the improper parts excised. The appellate court went on to hold that a magistrate could have reasonably inferred that the contraband found on defendant and in the passenger compartment established probable cause to believe the officers would find more in the trunk.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for the trial court to find, after further hearing if necessary, whether the officers would have sought a search warrant for the car's trunk even if they had not known of the truck's contents.


 

1424 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Woods v. Mitchell Bros. Truck Line, Inc.


No. 33094-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 449



February 26, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Woods v. Mitchell Bros. Truck Line, Inc., 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 521 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 26, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After respondent employer terminated appellant employee, the employee and his wife sued the employer for: (1) not paying overtime compensation under Wash. Rev. Code § 49.46.130(1); (2) wrongful withholding of wages under Wash. Rev. Code § 49.48.010; and (3) willful failure to pay wages under Wash. Rev. Code § 49.52.050(2). A Washington trial court granted the employer summary judgment and dismissed the complaint. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was an interstate truck driver. The employer asserted that the employee had never worked overtime within the state of Washington and that it had no obligation to pay him overtime for hours worked in other states. However, the appellate court held that a Washington-based employee had to be paid overtime even when the overtime hours accrued outside of the state. Although the employee was an Oregon resident, he was a Washington-based employee because: (1) the employer was a Washington corporation situated in Washington; (2) the employee traveled into Washington to the employer's terminal, where he was dispatched on his trucking routes; (3) when he finished a route, he would return to the Washington-based terminal, where he would file his bills of lading, await further dispatches, and receive his paychecks. Thus, his Oregon residency was irrelevant to his Washington-based employment. Such a holding did not violate the U.S. Constitution's commerce clause. However, because there was a bona fide wages dispute, the appellate court denied the employee's request for double damages under Wash. Rev. Code § 49.52.070.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment, awarded damages and prejudgment interest to the employee, and remanded for the trial court to determine the amount of attorney fees that the employee was entitled to recover for the proceedings below.

 

1425 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Armstrong


No. 57413-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


143 Wn. App. 333; 178 P.3d 1048; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 437



February 25, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Armstrong, 164 Wn.2d 1035, 197 P.3d 1185, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1216 (Wash., Nov. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 04-1-00541-4.SEA. Date filed in Superior Court: 11/9/05. Superior Court Judge Signing: Laura Inveen.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Superior Court, King County (Washington), found defendant guilty of second degree murder under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.32.050 and also found that he was armed with a deadly weapon during the commission of the crime. The trial judge sentenced him to 183 months of confinement, the low end of the standard range, plus a mandatory deadly weapon enhancement. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State treated differently similarly situated persons - those who committed an assault that resulted in death - by charging some of them with intentional murder and some of them with felony murder under the second degree murder statute. The felony murder statute was rationally related to the stated goal of punishing those who committed a homicide in the course of and in furtherance of a felony in the same manner as those who intended to kill. The elements of felony murder were the intent to shoot the victim with unlawful force with a deadly weapon, and causing the victim's death in the course of and in furtherance of the crime of assault. The elements of intentional murder were shooting the victim with the intent to cause the victim's death, and the shot causing the victim's death. The intent to commit the assault (which proximately caused death) and the intent to cause a death were different, requiring different proof. Because the intentional murder and felony murder statutes under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.32.050(1)(a) and (b) required proof of different elements, they did not violate the equal protection clauses in Wash. Const. art. I, § 12 and the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1426 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Joice


No. 57794-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 431



February 25, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Joice, 143 Wn. App. 1014, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 512 (2008)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree attempted murder with a firearm. The Washington trial court imposed an exceptional sentence after the jury found two aggravating circumstances. Defendant challenged the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized pursuant to a search warrant was properly denied where the supporting affidavits were specific about his activities and the incriminating items found during the search incident to his arrest. It was also reasonable to infer that evidence relating to his preparations would be found in defendant's locker at a gun shop where the evidence showed that he had created and test-fired a homemade silencer in preparation for the crime and had rented a locker at the gun shop several weeks before the shooting. The trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on lesser included offenses as first-degree assault was not a lesser included offense of attempted first degree murder. Application of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(3)(y) to defendant did not violate the ex post facto doctrine as the statutory aggravating circumstance was consistent with the legal principles previously established in case law. An exceptional sentence based on the victim's injuries was warranted as injury was not an element of first degree attempted murder. Finally, defendant's planning justified the exceptional sentence under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(3)(m).


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1427 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Moultrie


No. 58797-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


143 Wn. App. 387; 177 P.3d 776; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 413



February 25, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Moultrie, 164 Wn.2d 1035, 197 P.3d 1185, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1219 (2008)
Post-conviction relief granted at In re Pers. Restraint of Moultrie, 2015 Wash. App. LEXIS 499 (Wash. Ct. App., Mar. 9, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 05-1-11132-8.KNT. Date filed in Superior Court: September 5, 2006. Superior Court Judge Signing: Jay V. White.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Superior Court, King County (Washington), found defendant guilty of second degree rape for sexually assaulting a developmentally disabled woman. As a condition of his sentence, the trial court ordered that he have no contact with the victim, members of her family, and all vulnerable, ill, or disabled adults without the supervision of a responsible adult who had knowledge of his conviction. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's jury instruction adequately addressed the requirement of jury unanimity such that an ordinary juror would interpret it to mean that the jury had to be unanimous on the act underlying a conviction. However, the statutory terms "vulnerable adult" and "developmental disability" were more specific than the general terms "vulnerable" and "disabled" used in the no contact community placement condition. Because there was no indication that the trial court intended to limit the terms of the order to the statutory definitions in Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.44.010(16) and 71A.10.020(3), the appellate court would not presume it did so or otherwise rewrite the trial court's order. But, because ordinary people could differ about the meaning and application of the term "ill" adults, it had to be stricken from the no contact order as vague. Also, under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.712(5), defendant's community custody was equal to the remainder of his natural life once he was released from custody because the maximum term for the offense was life. Finally, the terms "vulnerable" and "disabled" adults accurately described the class of people victimized by defendant and were not overbroad.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, but remanded the case to the trial court to clarify the terms "vulnerable" and "disabled" in the no contact order and to strike the term "ill" from the no contact order.

 

1428 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin


No. 26041-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 428



February 19, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
County: SPOKANE COUNTY. Docket No(s): 97-1-00965-1. Judge signing: MICHAEL P. PRICE. Date filed: MARCH 30, 2007.
State v. Martin, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 501 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 19, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(b), appellant inmate, who was convicted in August 1997 of one count of first degree assault and two counts of reckless endangerment, moved for relief from judgment in March 2007. The Spokane County Superior Court, Washington, denied the inmate's motion. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that his judgment and sentence should be vacated because his offender score was miscalculated. The instant court concluded that the inmate's motion was untimely because it was filed well after the one-year time limit set forth in rule 7.8(b). The trial judge did not abuse his discretion by denying the inmate's motion for relief from judgment. The inmate's sentence was not facially invalid. The 1997 judgment and sentence, on its face, correctly reflected that the inmate's offender score was a 9 or more for each of the three counts sentenced. The sentencing court calculated the inmate's offender score by adding one point for each of the following: two other current offenses, one other current conviction listed under a different cause number, and eight prior convictions constituting criminal history. The score totaled 11 if each offense counted as one point. Even if two 1980 convictions and two 1983 convictions counted as one offense, as the inmate contended, his offender score would have been 9. Every ground that the inmate asserted was untimely, and every ground failed to satisfy any exception to Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090's one-year time limit.


OUTCOME: The order denying the inmate's motion for relief from judgment was affirmed.

 

1429 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kirkham


No. 57364-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 372



February 19, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Kirkham, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 407 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 19, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of a Washington trial court convicting him of third-degree assault in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.031(1)(g), malicious mischief in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.48.080, attempted escape in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.76.130(1), 9A.28.020(1), and third-degree rape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for beating his girlfriend, and after his arrest, attempting to escape from a police car and biting a detective. The trial court imposed terms of community custody of nine to 18 months for two counts of third-degree assault and third-degree rape and 36 to 48 months for third-degree rape. On appeal, the court held that because the terms of community custody exceeded the period allowed by Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.505(5), the case had to be remanded for resentencing. Defendant's convictions of third-degree assault and attempted escape did not violate his right against double jeopardy because the assault was not necessary to the attempted escape, as defendant would have committed acts providing the basis for his conviction of attempted escape even if he had not bitten the deputy. Defendant's convictions of malicious mischief and attempted escape did not violate defendant's right against double jeopardy because malicious mischief required proof of a different mental state, knowledge and malice, than attempted escape, intent to escape from custody. The seizure and admission into evidence of letters found in defendant's cell did not violate Wash. Const. art. 1, § 7.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The portion of defendant's sentence concerning community custody was reversed and the case was remanded for resentencing in such a fashion that any term of community custody imposed did not exceed the period of early release defendant earned.

In re Pers. Restraint of Lawrence


No. 59098-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 379



February 19, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Pers. Restraint of Lawrence, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 416 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Lawrence, 108 Wn. App. 226, 31 P.3d 1198, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1935 (2001)
State v. Lawrence, 107 Wn. App. 1045, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 3381 (2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of rape, and he had a prior New York conviction for attempted rape in the first degree. Defendant filed a personal restraint petition, seeking relief from his sentence of life in prison without the possibility of parole, imposed under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.030(27) (1997), Washington's "two strikes" law.


OVERVIEW: Although defendant showed that the trial court lacked statutory authority to analyze the facts of the New York conviction to see if it was comparable to a Washington two strikes offense, the fact remained that defendant's New York conviction was for a crime specifically listed in the two strikes statute. Counting defendant's New York conviction for attempted rape as a strike was not improper because the court could determine from the plain language of the statute that the conviction was for a listed offense.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

 

1431 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moynihan


No. 59325-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 380



February 19, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Moynihan, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 418 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 19, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to 25 counts of first degree theft, and stipulated to the facts in the State's certification of probable cause. A trial court, Washington, imposed an exceptional sentence of 108 months on all 25 counts to be served concurrently, but consecutive to any previously imposed sentence, with credit for time already served. Defendant appealed the imposition of the exceptional sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the exceptional sentence imposed under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(2)(c) violated his Sixth Amendment of the United States Constitution right to a jury trial. The trial court found that defendant had committed multiple current offenses, and that his high offender score would result in some of the current offenses going unpunished. It concluded as a matter of law that there were substantial and compelling reasons justifying an exceptional sentence. The trial court stated specifically that it was imposing an exceptional sentence under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(2)(c). Defendant stipulated to the facts, and agreed with the State's understanding of his criminal history and the calculation of his offender score. Under those circumstances, the court found that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(2)(c) permitted the judge to impose an exceptional sentence. The fact that the judge, rather than a jury, made the findings necessary to impose defendant's exceptional sentence did not implicate the Sixth Amendment.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

 

1432 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Braae


No. 25195-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 347



February 14, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Braae, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 401 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
County: YAKIMA. Docket No(s): 04-1-00807-2. Judge signing: C. JAMES LUST. Date filed: May 10, 2006.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Yakima County Superior Court, Washington, which convicted him of second degree malicious mischief and attempted second degree escape.


OVERVIEW: While incarcerated in a county jail, defendant removed the screen from his cell window and then used the screen to break the window. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying his proposed jury instruction regarding a constitutional right to outdoor exercise and in the definitional instruction of malice. The instant court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the proposed instruction because the instruction did not accurately state the law and was misleading and confusing. Although defendant was denied yard time, he did have access to the dayroom for indoor exercise. The record suggested both security and maintenance concerns were reasons for curbing outdoor exercise. Defendant's proposed instruction was merely theoretical. Moreover, this was not a civil suit over jail conditions, and no authority allowed an escapee to get fresh air or exercise. Although defendant claimed that the State failed to provide evidence to support an inference of malicious intent, the evidence showed defendant damaged jail property and laughed about it, creating an inference of malice. Thus, the evidence supported the instruction defining malice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Earl


No. 34632-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 340



February 12, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Earl, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 364 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 12, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Washington trial court, convicting him of one of two first-degree incest convictions, and his exceptional consecutive sentences for both convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of one count of third degree child rape, and two counts of first degree incest. On appeal defendant only challenged his conviction of first degree incest relating to his oldest daughter. The oldest daughter become pregnant, and blood tests showed that the likelihood ratio that defendant was the father was 640,000 to 1. The appellate court ruled that exhibit 2A, the blood draw form, was a non-testimonial business record. The blood draw form contained only verifiable facts, it did not contain an accusatory statement, cross examination would be impractical and unnecessary, and cross examination would not further the truth-seeking purpose of the Confrontation Clause. The admission of the document into evidence did not violate defendant's constitutional right to confront the witnesses against him. Also, the trial court did not violate defendant's equal protection rights in imposing his exceptional sentence. Defendant had not established that he was being treated differently than defendants who pled guilty or that his right to a jury trial was violated. Furthermore, defendant received notice that the State was seeking an exceptional sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Heath


No. 35056-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 341



February 12, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Heath, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 365 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 12, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the trial court (Washington), which convicted him of first-degree aggravated murder in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.95.020(7).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for the first-degree aggravated murder of his wife, but the appellate court affirmed, stating that the evidence was sufficient. He had access to the murder weapon and forensic experts identified the murder weapon; defendant was at the site of the victim's murder with the murder weapon; witnesses saw a dark-colored pickup truck at the murder scene shortly before the body was found; and defendant owned a blue pickup truck and was seen putting a rifle into the truck hours before the murder. The jury could have found that defendant was unhappy with his wife because he believed she was having an affair. Thus, viewed in favor of the State, the evidence was sufficient for the jury to convict defendant of murdering his wife. His argument that the aggravating factor charged by the State was void for vagueness was without merit because the State proved that defendant parked his truck fairly close to the victim's car. And he shot the victim from within five feet of her car. Under those circumstances, any reasonable person would have been on notice that he was firing from within the immediate vicinity of the vehicle he used to get to the scene with the weapon.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1435 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Dow


No. 34802-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


142 Wn. App. 971; 176 P.3d 597; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 283



February 5, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Dow, 164 Wn.2d 1007, 195 P.3d 87, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 859 (2008)
Reversed by State v. Dow, 2010 Wash. LEXIS 114 (Wash., Feb. 11, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Cowlitz Superior Court. Docket No. 05-1-01199-5. Judgment Date: 05/08/2006. Honorable Stephen M Warning, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with first degree child molestation, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.083(1). After the Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington) ruled that the victim was not competent to testify and that her statements to others were not admissible, it granted defendant's motion to suppress the statement he made during a police interview, held that Wash. Rev. Code § 10.58.035 was unconstitutional, and dismissed the charge. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that defendant's statement was trustworthy, but was inadmissible because the State failed to introduce independent evidence that criminal conduct at the core of the offense had occurred. However, the trial court failed to properly apply the factors set out in Wash. Rev. Code § 10.58.035 as the case law did not support its conclusion that corroboration was a federal constitutional requirement. Assuming arguendo that the corpus delicti rule was grounded in due process principles, the statute satisfied the core due process requirements by demanding some indication of reliability before an inculpatory statement was submitted to a jury. The statute also ensured that defendant could argue that the statement was not trustworthy or was otherwise insufficient to support a conviction. Thus, the statute was a lawful exercise of legislative authority and the trial court erred by refusing to analyze the admissibility of defendant's trustworthy statement under the factors set out in the statute.


OUTCOME: The dismissal was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court to apply each of the statutory factors to defendant's statement, determine the statement's admissibility, and conduct further hearings as appropriate.

State v. Glasmann


No. 34997-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 177



January 23, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court convicted defendant for second degree assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State failed to present sufficient evidence to prove the requisite intent to convict him of second degree assault. The appellate court found that the State presented sufficient evidence to establish that defendant intentionally touched the victim, thereby recklessly inflicting substantial bodily harm. A witness testified about the events she had observed from outside her motel room. The State also presented the 911 dispatch tape, which corroborated the witness's testimony. The appellate court deferred to the jury's finding defendant and the victim not credible. The jurors' inadvertent observations of defendant outside of the courtroom did not affect his right to a fair trial. Defendant was not entitled to an involuntary intoxication instruction as the record did not contain ample evidence that his level of intoxication affected his ability or lack thereof to form the mental state required to establish the crimes charged. Thus, defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel when his counsel failed to request an intoxication instruction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Fitzpatrick v. Okanogan County


No. 25161-6-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


143 Wn. App. 288; 177 P.3d 716; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 123



January 22, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Fitzpatrick v. Okanogan County, 164 Wn.2d 1008, 195 P.3d 86, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 855 (2008)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Fitzpatrick v. Okanogan County, 2010 Wash. LEXIS 716 (Wash., Sept. 2, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT DOUGLAS COUNTY. Superior Court No: 05-2-00235-0. Date filed in Superior Court: 4/13/06. Superior Court Judge signing: JOHN HOTCHKISS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sued respondent county and State, asserting an inverse condemnation claim for their land and homes that were swept down river during high waters, allegedly as a result of a blockage caused by a dike owned and maintained by the county and State. The Superior Court of Douglas County (Washington) granted the county and State summary judgment. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The common enemy doctrine did not insulate the county and State from damage caused by diking where the landowners had presented evidence that the waters held back by the dike would have otherwise flowed through natural side channels and rejoined the river. The character of the water was an issue of fact, and thus, the landowners had raised an issue of material fact as to whether the legal rule regarding riparian waters applied. Moreover, the landowners had presented evidence that the side channel drainways constituted flood channels under that legal rule. The county and State did not have immunity under Wash. Rev. Code §§ 86.12.037 and 86.16. 071 as the claim was for an unconstitutional taking; the landowners had not asserted a tort claim. The arguments that the governmental actions did not constitute a takings because the damage to the landowners' property was not contemplated by the county and State and it was not necessarily incident to the construction of the dike were rejected as the unintended results of governmental activity could constitute a taking. The landowners had also presented issues of fact as to the county's and State's roles with respect to dike.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment was reversed. The case was remanded.

State v. Newlun


No. 58762-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


142 Wn. App. 730; 176 P.3d 529; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 164



January 22, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at State v. Newlun, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 863 (Wash., Sept. 4, 2008)
Review denied by State v. Newlun, 165 Wn.2d 1007, 198 P.3d 513, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1097 (2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at In re Pers. Restraint of Newlun, 2010 Wash. App. LEXIS 2259 (Wash. Ct. App., Oct. 4, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: Snohomish. Superior Court Cause No: 06-1-00241-0. Date filed in Superior Court: August 14, 2006 and August 11, 2006. Superior Court Judge Signing: The Honorable Richard J. Thorpe.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Snohomish County (Washington), convicted defendant, upon a plea of guilty, of 11 counts in three separate cause numbers. The trial court found the aggravating factor set forth in Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(2)(c) to be satisfied and premised the imposition of an exceptional sentence on the existence of that factor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(2)(c) allowed the trial court to impose an exceptional sentence on the basis of a factual finding that, under the Sixth Amendment as interpreted in Blakely, was the sole province of the jury. Thus, defendant contended that the trial court unconstitutionally applied Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(2)(c) when it imposed an exceptional sentence. Defendant's convictions for the multiple current offenses for which he was sentenced were each individually subject to the right of trial by jury and to the requirement of proof beyond a reasonable doubt. Those same convictions, in combination with defendant's prior convictions, resulted in his high offender score. Those factors, in turn, provided the basis for the trial court's imposition of an exceptional sentence pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(2)(c). Because the fact of defendant's criminal convictions provided the sole basis for the imposition of his exceptional sentence, he failed to meet his burden of showing that the trial court's application of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(2)(c) violated the Sixth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court, Yakima County, Washington, found defendant guilty of first degree rape of a child. As a condition of his community custody, defendant could not possess, view, or purchase pornography. He appealed this condition of community custody.
