State v. Brooks


No. 35292-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 81



January 15, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Brooks, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 115 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 15, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court convicted defendant of first degree escape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support his first degree escape conviction because the State failed to prove an essential element of first degree escape--that he escaped from lawful custody when the deputy attempted to arrest him based on the electronic Department of Corrections (DOC) warrant. The appellate court found that because the deputy was allowed to rely on the DOC's information indicating that defendant had an outstanding arrest warrant, this information gave him probable cause to arrest; when defendant escaped from the deputy, he was under lawful arrest based on the electronic DOC arrest warrant. Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.76.110(1) required and the instructions supported proof of a single mental state--"knowing" escape from custody. Instruction 10 was proper as its definition of "lawful arrest" neither commented on the evidence nor directed a verdict. The trial court did not err in refusing to define "arrest." Defendant's motion to suppress his escape was denied as it occurred after the deputy discovered the warrant and informed defendant. Defendant's motion for mistrial was denied. Defendant failed to establish ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Fualaau


No. 52043-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 55



January 14, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Fualaau, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 261 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Fualaau, 148 P.3d 1044, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 8 (Wash., 2007)
State v. Fualaau, 126 Wn. App. 1011, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1089 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the trial court (Washington), which imposed an exceptional sentence upward for possession of a firearm in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41040(1)(a), (2)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his exceptional sentence upward for possession of a firearm and the appellate court vacated the exceptional sentence and remanded for resentencing. The trial court imposed an exceptional sentence on defendant based upon the severity of the victim's injuries. Defendant's stipulation did not explicitly state that the facts stipulated to form a legal basis for an exceptional sentence. He did not explicitly stipulate that the victim's injuries were severe. Further, a jury did not find beyond a reasonable doubt that the victim's injuries were severe. While the factual record implied that the injuries were severe, that was not sufficient to meet the requirements of the Sixth Amendment right to trial by jury. Thus, the trial court erred when it imposed an exceptional sentence based on the severity of the victim's injuries.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the exceptional sentence and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Calhoun


No. 34941-8-II consolidated with No. 34983-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 31



January 8, 2008, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals February 27, 2008. RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Calhoun, 142 Wn. App. 1022, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 84 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 8, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants sought review of the decision of the trial court (Washington), which convicted them of first-degree robbery, first-degree burglary, and two counts of second-degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendants appealed their convictions for first-degree robbery, first-degree burglary, and two counts of second-degree assault and the appellate court affirmed in part but reversed the second-degree assault convictions. The trial court did not err in allowing evidence of a showup identification, in part because sufficient evidence supported the conviction even without the pretrial identification. Defendants did not contend that the pretrial identification tainted the subsequent in-court identification by the victims. Thus, the admission of the pretrial identification was merely cumulative evidence. The trial court did not err in determining that the first defendant understood the nature of the charges and had the ability to assist his defense because a colloquy demonstrated that he could articulate and understand the nature of the charges, as well as the roles of the judge, prosecutor, and counsel. The second-degree assault convictions were improper because neither the trial testimony, the State's closing argument, nor the jury instructions referred to, or indicated to, an independent purpose of design that would have separated the robbery from the assault on that victim.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the convictions for first-degree burglary and first-degree robbery, but reversed both second-degree assault convictions and remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

State v. Alphonse


No. 58449-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


142 Wn. App. 417; 174 P.3d 684; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 12



January 7, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Remanded by State v. Alphonse, 164 Wn.2d 1021, 196 P.3d 134, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1019 (2008)
Remanded by State v. Alphonse, 147 Wn. App. 891, 197 P.3d 1211, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 3031 (Wash. Ct. App., Dec. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: Snohomish. Superior Court Cause No: 06-1-00426-9. Date filed in Superior Court: 6/9/06. Superior Court Judge Signing: Gerald Knight.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Snohomish County Superior Court (Washington) convicting him of felony and misdemeanor telephone harassment in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.61.230. Defendant was also ordered not to have any contact with the victim and was ordered not to appear within the city's limits unless required for legal or judicial reasons.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for leaving a threatening message on the voice mail of the victim, a police officer, who had previously investigated defendant. On appeal, the court held that § 9.61.230 did not require the State to prove that the caller had the intent to harass, intimidate, torment, or embarrass at the time the call was placed, and therefore the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because there was ample evidence that he had the requisite intent at many times during the telephone call. Prosecuting defendant for making calls that were allegedly a lawful petition to a government official for redress of grievances did not violate his First Amendment rights because while defendant may have been legally voicing disapproval about the way in which the victim handled the investigation, once he used speech to harass, intimidate, torment, or embarrass the victim, his conduct became criminal. The court vacated the order banishing defendant from the city because it was not narrowly tailored to serve the State's interest in protecting the safety of the victim and other police officers.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but the banishment order was vacated.

State v. Vance


No. 55364-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


142 Wn. App. 398; 174 P.3d 697; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 14



January 7, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at State v. Vance, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 977 (Wash., Oct. 1, 2008)
Review granted by State v. Vance, 165 Wn.2d 1036, 205 P.3d 131, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 375 (2009)
Reversed by State v. Vance, 2010 Wash. LEXIS 432 (Wash., May 6, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: Snohomish. Superior Court Cause No: 02-1-02090-3. Date filed in Superior Court: November 9, 2004. Superior Court Judge Signing: The Honorable Larry E. McKeeman.
State v. Vance, 159 Wn.2d 1011, 152 P.3d 1032, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 146 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of multiple counts of child molestation, three in the first degree and two in the second degree, and of communication with a minor for immoral purposes. He was resentenced to consecutive sentences for the offenses, pursuant to former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(2)(i) (2003). The sentence was affirmed on appeal. Review was granted, and the Supreme Court of Washington remanded for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Child molestation in the first degree was not established by statute as a serious violent offense. Pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.589(a)(1), consecutive sentences for felonies not established as serious violent offenses could only be imposed under the exceptional sentence provisions of former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535. Defendant argued that the exceptional sentences violated Blakely because the judge, rather than the jury, conducted the fact finding necessary to justify them. Based on the supreme court's holding in the Matter of the Personal Restraint of VanDelft, the court agreed. When the trial court imposed consecutive sentences of confinement for convictions for multiple felonies that were not defined as serious violent offenses, it imposed exceptional sentences. The sentences were premised upon the trial court's determination that the imposition of concurrent sentences would result in punishment that was clearly too lenient. Because the U.S. Constitution required that such a finding be made by a jury, rather than by a judge, and no procedure existed at the time of defendant's convictions for his jury to make such a finding, the sentences had to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the challenged sentences, ordered them vacated, and remanded the case to the trial court with directions that standard range sentences be imposed upon him. The State could not seek an exceptional sentence on remand.

Outlook Ridge LLC v. Cross Valley Water Dist.


No. 59102-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 17



January 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Outlook Ridge, LLC v. Cross Valley Water Dist., 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 65 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 7, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners entered into a developer extension agreement with respondent water district. The owners sued the district to obtain a refund of a water connection fee, alleging that the district did not have the authority under former Wash. Rev. Code § 57.08.005(10) to require the owners to pay a fee. A trial court, Washington, granted the district's motion for summary judgment, and dismissed the lawsuit. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners contended that because they were not connected to the district's "existing" water system and the water was supplied by another water district, the district did not have the authority to impose a water connection fee. Former Wash. Rev. Code § 57.08.005(10) explicitly authorized the district the right to impose a connection charge on property owners seeking to connect to the district's systems, as a condition to granting the right to so connect. The court found that the plain language of the statute did not limit a connection charge to the cost of an "existing system." The district had the exclusive authority to provide water service to the area and to the owners. The district's comprehensive plan approved construction of a project in order to provide additional capacity to serve the area. As agreed in a developer extension agreement, the district owned the water lines that connected the owners to the water supply. And, the water the district temporarily purchased from the other district was provided to the owners through a water system owned and operated by the district. Thus, the district had the authority to impose a water connection fee under § 57.08.005(10).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Glover v. Alaska


No. 59622-5


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


142 Wn. App. 442; 174 P.3d 1246; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 18; 2008 AMC 177



January 7, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Glover v. State, 175 P.3d 1240, 2008 Alas. LEXIS 9 (Alaska, Jan. 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: Whatcom. Superior Court Cause No: 05-2-02811-1. Date filed in Superior Court: February 2, 2007. Superior Court Judge Signing: Ira J. Uhrig.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker sued respondent Department of Transportation, Alaska Marine Highway System, pursuant to the Jones Act, seeking to recover damages and a declaratory judgment that Alaska Stat. § 09.50.250(5) violated the Alaska and United States constitutions. An Alaskan superior court entered an order granting Alaska's motion for summary judgment. The Superior Court, Whatcom, Washington, declined to exercise jurisdiction. The worker appealed.


OVERVIEW: The worker was a resident of Alaska. The worker was injured while working aboard an Alaska state ferry. At the time of the worker's injury, the ferry was in the approaches to Cordova harbor, within Alaska's territorial waters. The Washington superior court action was filed 10 days before summary judgment was granted in the Alaskan matter, but the two cases were identical. Alaska moved to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction pursuant to Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 12(b)(1) on the theory that Alaska's sovereign immunity in its own courts as to Jones Act claims pursuant to Alaska Stat. § 09.50.250(5) also removed the Washington superior court's power to hear such claims brought against Alaska. Alaska's motion also separately contended that the superior court should decline to exercise jurisdiction on the basis of interstate comity. The Washington court properly declined to exercise jurisdiction over claims brought against Alaska, as a sister state. The matter was still pending before the Alaska Supreme Court, and declining to exercise jurisdiction would allow the Alaska the first opportunity to examine the constitutional validity of its own rules and regulations.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In re Dependency of T.S.S.


No. 58575-4-I Consolidated with/No. 58871-1; No. 58576-2; No. 58870-2


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 22



January 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Dependency of T.S.S., 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 60 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 7, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants parents appealed the judgment of a Washington trial court that terminated their parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued, inter alia, that the State did not prove that all services capable of correcting parental deficiencies had been offered. The court of appeals disagreed. Because the mother did not engage in the services that were offered and provided, the mother's argument that the State had to provide additional services failed. The parental deficiency that necessitated removal of the children was chronic neglect of the children that jeopardized their health, safety, and welfare. The State offered and provided the mother numerous services over a three-year period, including parenting classes, therapeutic day care, and counseling with two different family preservation service therapists. The mother agreed to complete parenting classes and obtain a psychological evaluation to identify any other parenting deficiencies that the State could address. But the mother did not follow through with any of the services the State offered or provided and both therapists eventually terminated services because the mother cancelled and missed so many appointments. Substantial evidence supported the trial court's finding that it would have been futile to offer additional services.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Faust v. Albertson


No. 57821-9-I Consolidated with No. 57321-7-I Linked with No. 57320-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


143 Wn. App. 272; 178 P.3d 358; 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 37



January 7, 2008, Filed


NOTICE: Order Granting Motion to Publish February 25, 2008.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at Faust v. Albertson, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 864 (Wash., Sept. 4, 2008)
Review granted by Faust v. Albertson, 164 Wn.2d 1025, 196 P.3d 136, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1021 (2008)
Reversed by Faust v. Mark Albertson, 211 P.3d 400, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 724 (Wash., July 16, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Faust v. Albertson, 142 Wn. App. 1020, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 83 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a bartender and a bar, appealed the judgment rendered in a Washington trial court that found them liable for negligently overserving alcohol to defendant decedent who injured respondents, vehicle occupants, in an automobile accident. Respondents cross-appealed contending that the interest rate on tort judgments violated their constitutional right to equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that the evidence as to overserving was insufficient to sustain the verdict. The court of appeals agreed. Witnesses testified that the bartender admitted that the decedent was drunk when he left the bar. That did not prove overservice. The bartender's statements, as related by the witnesses, was not sufficient evidence to forestall a directed verdict. That evidence was not sufficient to establish the decedent's appearance at the time of service of alcohol. Because the purpose was to protect against foreseeable hazards resulting from service to an intoxicated person, the duty only applied to the service of alcohol to those already exhibiting signs of the influence of alcohol. The bar could not be held liable when a patron was not "apparently under the influence" when served. As long as the bartender did not serve the decedent after he "appeared" under the influence, neither she, nor the bar, were liable for respondents' injuries. Since, no evidence described the decedent's state of intoxication when the bartender served him, substantial evidence did not support the verdict against appellants for overservice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and vacated. The cross-appeal was denied.

 

1449 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


No. 57021-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3346



December 31, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Davis, 142 Wn. App. 1017, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3359 (Wash. Ct. App., Dec. 31, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to one count of rape of a child in the second degree. Based on defendant's criminal history, a trial court, Washington, sentenced defendant to a maximum term of life and a minimum term of 129 months in prison. He received community custody for life upon release from confinement. The trial court adopted 21 community custody conditions. Defendant brought a pre-enforcement challenge to two of the conditions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that two of his community custody provisions were unconstitutionally vague. Claims of vagueness were better assessed after enforcement, with a record of specific conduct. The court affirmed a prior decision to forgo facial challenges for vagueness on sentencing conditions. Defendant claimed that a prohibition against possessing pornography and visiting establishments whose primary business pertained to sexually explicit or erotic material was overbroad because no nexus existed between his crime and the condition. The circumstances of the sexual assault reflected defendant's inability to regulate his sexual behavior. Limiting defendant's access to sexually stimulating materials was proper under the Washington Sentencing Reform Act and not overbroad. Defendant's sentence included the requirement that he not possess or control any item designated or used to entertain, attract, or lure children. The intent to use these items to make contact with children, not their mere possession, related to the circumstances of the crime of second degree rape of a child. Without intent, the prohibition did not qualify as an appropriate crime-related prohibition under the Act.


OUTCOME: The prohibitions against pornography and frequenting establishments whose primary business pertained to sexually explicit or erotic material were affirmed. The condition concerning defendant's possession or control of items designated or used to entertain, attract, or lure children was remanded for clarification with respect to intent.

State v. J.H.


No. 25335-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3319



December 27, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Superior Court County: OKANOGAN. Docket No(s): 06-8-00082-3. Judge signing: DAVID S. EDWARDS, JUDGE PRO TEM. Date filed: June 7, 2006.
State v. J.H., 142 Wn. App. 1016, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3353 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Superior Court, Okanogan County (Washington), defendant was convicted of harassment under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.020 for making a threatening remark to his teacher. Defendant appealed, arguing that the State failed to prove the elements of the crime charged.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a high school student, stated to his teacher, "If you send me back to juvey, I will make your life hell." At the time, defendant was very agitated, angry, and forceful. Defendant argued that his statement did not rise to the level of harassment for purposes of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.020 because it was not a direct threat of bodily harm and it would not have placed a reasonable person in fear of bodily harm. The appellate court disagreed, noting that: (1) the threat was made in a small conference room with two adults present; (2) defendant made the statement while in an agitated and angry state, a context which established that the statement was not made in jest but, rather, was a serious threat; and (3) the statement placed the teacher in reasonable fear of bodily injury, as the record provided sufficient evidence of defendant's history of physical violence and his threatening behaviors at the time the statement was made.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

In re Pers. Restraint of Bybee


No. 35438-1-II, Consolidated with No. 36660-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


142 Wn. App. 260; 175 P.3d 589; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3311



December 24, 2007, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Inmates sought relief from personal restraint imposed by the Washington trial court after each pled guilty to first degree kidnapping (with a firearm sentencing enhancement), first degree robbery, two counts of first degree burglary, and first degree unlawful possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: The inamtes' judgment and sentence became final on July 17, 2000 and November 30, 2000, respectfully, when the appellate court issued mandates disposing of their respective direct appeals. Both inmates filed personal restraint petitions (PRPs), which were consolidated. Both inmates sought dismissal of their kidnapping convictions as incidental to their robbery convictions. The appellate court found that the inmates filed their PRPs more than one year after their respective judgments became final, and the PRPs did not fall within an exemption or an exception to the one-year limit. The inmates' claim for relief did not satisfy the time-bar exceptions for convictions under an unconstitutional statute as applied, for double jeopardy violations, for sentences in excess of jurisdiction, or for a significant change in merger law. Also, when the inmates pled guilty to both kidnapping and robbery, they admitted a sufficient factual basis for both charges. The inmates' guilty pleas barred them from claiming insufficient evidence based on caselaw incidental restraint analysis.


OUTCOME: The requests for relief were denied.

 

1452 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Murawski


No. 56941-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


142 Wn. App. 278; 173 P.3d 994; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3316



December 24, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Murawski, 164 Wn.2d 1005, 190 P.3d 55, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 778 (Wash., Aug. 5, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 04-1-00561-9.SEA. Date filed in Superior Court: 7/18/05. Superior Court Judge Signing: Sharon S. Armstrong.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the King County Superior Court, Washington, granted defendant's motion to strike the aggravating facts from the State's amended information, defendant pled guilty to the original charge of first degree theft. The State's motion to impanel a jury to prove the aggravating facts necessary to support an exceptional sentence was denied. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State contended the sentencing court erroneously refused to impanel a jury under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.537, believing that it lacked the authority to do so because defendant committed her crime before the legislature enacted § 9.94A.537. The appellate court agreed, finding that a recent state supreme court's decision held that § 9.94A.537 applied to all criminal cases where trials had not begun or pleas had not been accepted before its effective date. And contrary to defendant's assertion, double jeopardy considerations did not apply because no judge or jury had even considered, much less acquitted, defendant of the allegations on which the aggravating circumstances were based. The sentencing court's refusal to use the recently enacted statutory procedure to consider whether any aggravating circumstances applied could not be characterized as a resolution of guilt or innocence, and the State was not seeking to punish defendant twice for the same criminal conduct. The State merely sought to use the correct procedure for determining defendant's punishment by considering the aggravating circumstances for the first time.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was reversed and remanded for sentencing in accordance with Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.537.

 

1453 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Bishop v. City of Spokane


No. 25684-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


142 Wn. App. 165; 173 P.3d 318; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3258



December 18, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT, SPOKANE COUNTY. Superior Court No: 05-2-03137-3. Superior Court Judge signing: HAROLD D. CLARKE. Date filed in Superior Court: OCTOBER 26, 2006.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A police officer was parked in front of appellant arrestee's driveway. After he refused to move his patrol car and told her that he would deal with her later, she drove around the officer's car. He then arrested her for obstructing a law enforcement officer. Subsequently, she filed a suit for false arrest. The Superior Court, Spokane County (Washington) granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment and dismissed her case. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee's truck was sitting on her driveway when the police stopped another vehicle. The officer parked his patrol car in front of her driveway. She tried to talk to the officer and have him move his car, but he told her to shut up and back up and that he would deal with her later. She then drove across a blacktopped portion of her front yard and around the officer. He stopped and then arrested her. She was charged with obstructing a law enforcement officer under Seattle, Wash., Mun. Code § 10.07.032. The appellate court stated that more was required of the arrestee than driving around a parked car after an officer told her to shut up and that he would deal with her later to find that she obstructed the officer, or, at least, there was a genuine issue of material fact as to whether her actions of driving around the patrol car obstructed the officer in his official duties. Thus, there was a genuine issue of material fact as to whether the officer had probable cause to believe that the arrestee knowingly or willfully acted to obstruct the law enforcement officer in his official duties as required. Therefore, the trial court erred in granting the city's summary judgment motion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment summarily dismissing the arrestee's claim and remanded the case for trial.

 

1454 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Pers. Restraint of Mattson


No. 58823-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


142 Wn. App. 130; 172 P.3d 719; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3250



December 17, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by, Request granted In re Pers. Restraint of Mattson, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 479 (Wash. Ct. App., Mar. 3, 2008)
Reversed by In re Pers. Restraint of Mattson, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 735 (Wash., Aug. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 98-1-09413-0.SEA. Date filed in Superior Court: September 15, 2006.
State v. Mattson, 117 Wn. App. 1050, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2004 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate, a sex offender, was denied a transfer to community custody in lieu of earned early release. The inmate filed a personal restraint petition challenging the policies of the Washington Department of Corrections that categorically prevented approval of a proposed release plan transferring the inmate to community custody if a forensic evaluation found that he met the criteria for civil commitment as a sexually violent predator.


OVERVIEW: The Department's policy categorically prevented approval of a sex offender's release plan if a forensic evaluation determined that the inmate met the criteria of a sexually violent predator because no proposed community release plan would be deemed sufficiently safe to ensure community protection. Neither the current nor the former versions of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.728 authorized the Department to categorically exempt sex offenders who meet the criteria of sexually violent predators, nor did the statute allow the Department to decide to refuse to approve a release plan because no community release address, absent one with a 24/7 prison-like monitoring and lock-down, would be safe enough to protect the community. Even if a forensic evaluation concluded that the inmate met the criteria of a sexually violent predator, 24/7 prison-like monitoring and lock-down could only be accomplished within the constraints of due process by means of a civil commitment proceeding. Until then, the Department could not categorically exempt a sex offender like the inmate from consideration for transfer to community custody and had to evaluate his proposed release plan on its merits.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted the inmate's personal restraint petition and directed the Department to evaluate his most recently proposed release plan and residence on its merits.

 

1455 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


No. 58698-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3240



December 10, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Davis, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3261 (Wash. Ct. App., Dec. 10, 2007)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the trial court (Washington) of two counts of obtaining a signature by deception or duress, four counts of offering a false instrument for filing or recording, six counts of theft in the first degree, one count of forgery, and one count of identity theft in the first degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised many issues on appeal, but the court affirmed. The to-convict instructions for each of four counts of offering false instrument for filing or record could have been read as a direction or as a comment by the trial court that the documents referenced were false instruments. However, the error was harmless because the record was replete with evidence that the instruments were false and no juror could have found that the documents were not false instruments, and thus no showing of prejudice was made. The statutory aggravating factor was that defendant knew or should have known that the victim was vulnerable under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(3)(b), and the jury was properly instructed that it had to find this factor proved beyond a reasonable doubt, and thus the requirements of case law were satisfied. All the elements of the crime and the enhanced sentence factor were proven beyond a reasonable doubt, thus satisfying due process concerns, and because the findings were made by a unanimous jury, this satisfied U.S. Amend. VI concerns. Defendant failed to demonstrate that the venire selection process failed to comply with the requirements of the applicable statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

In re Marriage of Garth


NO. 58815-0-I, 58983-1-I, 59319-6-I (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3243



December 10, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Marriage of Garth, 142 Wn. App. 1007, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3262 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged an order of a trial court (Washington), which modified the parties' parenting plan pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.191 by limiting the residential time the father spent with the children and giving respondent mother all decision-making authority based upon the father's physical and emotional abuse of the children. The trial court awarded the mother attorney's fees and refused to seal the records.


OVERVIEW: The father allegedly physically and emotionally abused his children. The trial court found that there was an impairment of emotional ties between the father and his children, which interfered with his performance of parenting functions. The father displayed dominant, manipulative and intimidating behavior. On appeal, the court found that the terms "abuse" and "impairment" in § 26.09.191 were inherently serious and not unconstitutionally vague because Wash. Rev. Code § 26.44.015 distinguished between abuse and reasonable corporal punishment. A doctor testified that the father was severely controlling, and the father admitted that he had an anger management problem. The father did not establish that his interest in securing employment outweighed the right of the public to open judicial proceedings to support sealing the records. The imposition of attorney's fees was proper when the father used the courts as a means of perpetuating his need to intimidate and he took inconsistent positions with respect to the same factual events. However, the trial court should have reduced the fees by the amount that the mother admitted were erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment modifying the parenting plan and denying the motion to seal or redact the findings regarding abuse, but the court remanded the action for a recalculation of attorney fees.

State v. Burrows


NO. 58946-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3238



December 10, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Burrows, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3266 (Wash. Ct. App., Dec. 10, 2007)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from a trial court (Washington), which denied his motion to dismiss and convicted him of failure to register as a sex offender, contrary to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.130(5)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to first-degree child molestation when he was 13 years old. As a result of the conviction, he was required to register as a sex offender under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.130. The State later charged him with failure to register when he moved, in violation of § 9A.44.130(5)(a). Defendant moved to dismiss the charge, arguing that the statute provided insufficient procedural due process for a sex offender who registered a change of address. He asserted that the statute needed to require the sheriff to provide a registrant with a receipt or other confirmation. Defendant was convicted of the charge. On appeal, the court found that defendant did not show that the lack of a copy requirement in the statutory registration procedures was a deficiency that deprived a sex offender of a liberty or property interest, in violation of Wash. Const. art. 1, § 3. Defendant did not show that the registration requirement infringed upon his right to travel. While prudence might dictate that an offender request a copy or other confirmation of registration, there was no constitutional necessity for the sheriff to offer such protection because no state deprivation of liberty occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1458 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 58648-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3189



December 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Williams, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3212 (Wash. Ct. App., Dec. 3, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the trial court (Washington) of, in part, first degree burglary with a firearm and second degree assault with a firearm. Defendant had pleaded guilty to one count of unlawful possession of a firearm. Defendant appealed and the State also appealed, challenging the trial court's imposition of a concurrent firearm enhancement on the second degree assault count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the State raised various arguments. The court affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part. The court disagreed with defendant's claim that the information regarding burglary was insufficient, for purposes of U.S. Const. amend. VI and Wash. Const. art. I, § 22. The information mirrored Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.52.020(1). Under the statute, unlawfully entering or remaining in a building was an essential element of burglary. While ownership or occupancy might have been necessary to prove that entry was unlawful, neither ownership nor occupancy was an essential element of burglary, as defendant argued. The court disagreed that the in-court identification was tainted by an impermissibly suggestive pretrial identification procedure. Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.6 did not apply and the motion to exclude the identification was properly denied. Defendant's guilty plea to unlawful possession of a firearm was involuntary and the court reversed the conviction and remanded for defendant to plead anew. The trial court acted outside its statutory authority when it imposed a concurrent, rather than consecutive, firearm enhancement to his conviction of second degree assault.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the sentence on the second degree assault count and remanded for a new sentence. The court reversed the conviction for unlawful possession of a firearm and remanded for defendant to plead to that count anew. The court affirmed the burglary conviction.

Lee's Drywall Co. v. Dep't of Labor & Indus.


No. 35613-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


141 Wn. App. 859; 173 P.3d 934; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3161


October 9, 2007, Oral Argument 
November 27, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Thurston Superior Court. Docket No: 06-2-00590-0. Date filed: October 27, 2006. Judge signing: Honorable Wm. Thomas Mcphee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Washington Department of Labor & Industries, ordered appellant contractor to pay the industrial insurance premiums that a subcontractor did not pay under Wash. Rev. Code § 51.12.070. The Washington Board of Industrial Insurance Appeals adopted the industrial appeals judge's decision affirming the Department's order. The Thurston Superior Court (Washington) affirmed the Board's decision. The contractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The contractor presented no evidence that the subcontractor maintained a principal place of business, on the owner's kitchen table or anywhere else, that the owner used exclusively to conduct the subcontractor's business. Also, the regular invoices and cancelled checks supported a conclusion that the subcontractor maintained records of at least its dealings with the contractor, but the Department's auditor testified that the owner did not produce a complete set of records for the audit. Also, the contractor produced no further evidence that the subcontractor maintained records of all income, including income from sources other than the contractor, or any business expenses. Thus, the trial court did not err in finding that the contractor did not present sufficient evidence to prove that the subcontractor maintained a separate set of books and records that reflected all items of income and expenses of the business. Therefore, the Board did not err in finding that the subcontractor did not meet the requirements for the prime contractor liability exception. Accordingly, the Department did not err in seeking the subcontractor's unpaid industrial insurance premiums from the contractor.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Idland


No. 59129-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3133



November 26, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Idland, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3176 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 26, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court denied defendant's motion to terminate the legal financial obligations imposed by the trial court after he was convicted of three counts of custodial sexual misconduct in the second degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(b), defendant moved to strike the costs of the incarceration provision of his sentence because the trial court had failed to ascertain whether or not defendant had the financial means to meet those costs. The appellate court noted that when defendant entered his Alford plea, he was aware he would be assessed costs and fines. Although defendant was aware that the State recommended financial obligations at the time of sentencing, he neither objected to those costs nor put forth evidence regarding his inability to pay. Unless the State was seeking to collect those costs, the time to object to the imposition of that fine was then. Wash. Rev. Code § 10.01.160(4) entitled a defendant to petition the court for modification or remission of the court-imposed costs if making payments imposed a manifest hardship on the defendant. Indeed, post-sentencing, the issue of the costs may not be ripe for review until the State attempted to collect them. A trial court in exercising its discretion to impose costs did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Holmes


No. 57875-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3132



November 26, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Holmes, 141 Wn. App. 1040, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3163 (2007)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a Washington trial court of four counts of felony telephone harassment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions because there was insufficient evidence for the jury to find that the threats were true threats or that he had the requisite intent to harass, intimidate, or torment his victims. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant made at least nine calls to four victims on the same day and during the same general time period. Each call began almost immediately with a threatening tirade predicated on defendant's dismissal from employment. Nothing in the record suggested that the calls had any purpose other than to harass and intimidate the victims. Defendant's obsession with his expulsion over a long period of time, his express vendetta against his victims, the angry tone of his threats, his appearance at the home of one victim, and his escalation to describing exactly how he would kill his victims all supported the conclusion that a reasonable person in his position would have foreseen his listeners taking his threats seriously. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Det. of Johnson


No. 57240-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3088



November 19, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Det. of Johnson, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3116 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from Snohomish Superior Court. Docket No: 98-2-00133-8. Date filed: 10/24/2005. Judge signing: Honorable George N Bowden.
In re Det. of Thorell, 149 Wn.2d 724, 72 P.3d 708, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 463 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Snohomish Superior Court, Washington, granted the State's motion to strike the trial date where the legislature amended the statute governing sexually violent predator (SVP) annual order to show cause hearings to preclude granting a new trial solely on the basis of a change of single demographic factor, including age. Appellant patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued that striking his trial date constituted retroactive application of new legislation in violation of the separation of powers doctrine. The appellate court found that a prior court determined that a vested right, entitled to protection from legislation, had to be something more than a mere expectation based upon an anticipated continuance of the existing law. An expectation that there would be no change in the SVP criteria under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.090 did not vest existing SVPs with a right to have recommitment hearing requests evaluated according to the pre-2005 criteria. The amended statute applied to the patient prospectively, not retrospectively as a trial had not yet been held. The application of the statutory amendment did not violate the patient's due process rights. An SVP retained adequate procedural protections to safeguard against commitment if and when they no longer met the criteria of an SVP.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1463 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


No. 55347-0-1


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3089



November 19, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Brown, 141 Wn. App. 1034, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3114 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a Washington trial court of seven counts of possession of depictions of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct with sexual motivation. An exceptional sentence was imposed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that because a polygraph was not a condition of his community placement, the department of corrections (DOC) did not have the authority to conduct a polygraph. The court of appeals disagreed. There was no dispute that the trial court required defendant to participate in "crime-related treatment or counseling services as directed by the department" as a condition of community placement. While incarcerated, defendant enrolled in a sex offender treatment program. The aftercare phase of the program occurred during community placement and the treatment contract required periodic polygraph examinations to monitor compliance. Therefore, the DOC had the authority to require polygraph examinations as part of the treatment program that was expressly imposed by the trial court. Additionally, to establish chain of custody for fingerprint evidence on a DVD disk, the State presented the testimony of the court clerk and security officers who were present during the first trial. The witnesses testified that they did not see defendant touch the DVD. Therefore, the trial court's decision to admit fingerprint testimony about the DVD was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The exceptional sentence was reversed and the case was remanded for resentencing. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

McAllister v. City of Bellevue Firemen's Pension Bd.


No. 57869-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


142 Wn. App. 250; 180 P.3d 786; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3098



November 19, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: Order Granting Motion to Publish December 17, 2007.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by McAllister v. City of Bellevue Firemen's Pension Bd., 164 Wn.2d 1002, 190 P.3d 54, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 809 (2008)
Affirmed by McAllister v. City of Bellevue Firemen's Pension Bd., 166 Wn.2d 623, 210 P.3d 1002, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 637 (Wash., July 9, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: McAllister v. City of Bellevue Firemen's Pension Bd., 141 Wn. App. 1035, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3118 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant firefighters challenged a decision of respondent city firemen's pension board, which prospectively calculated the benefits they would have received under their prior pension plan under Wash. Rev. Code ch. 41.18 (1955 Act) using the 1955 Act salary definition instead of the definition under Wash. Rev. Code ch. 41.26. The firefighters also challenged the denial of their writ of review by the superior court (Washington).


OVERVIEW: After the firefighters retired, the city determined that excess payments were incorrectly calculated. The pension board found that the city miscalculated pension benefits and the superior court denied a writ of review. The court affirmed. Under the plain language of Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26.040(2), the firefighters had the right to be treated as if they retired under the 1955 Act. Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26.040(2) required the pension board to calculate the benefits under the 1955 Act and then compare that to what the firefighters would receive under the Law Enforcement Officers' and Fire Fighters' System Pension Plan (LEOFF), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 41.26. If the amount was greater under the 1955 Act, they were entitled to an excess benefit payment under Wash. Rev. Code. § 41.26.040(2). The city had to use the 1955 Act salary definition under Wash. Rev. Code § 41.18.030 to calculate the amount the firefighters would have received to determine whether they were entitled to an excess payment. Because the legislature amended Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26.040(2) before the LEOFF retirement system took effect, the firefighters did not have the right to the contribution rate under the 1955 Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1465 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Russell


No. 34424-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


141 Wn. App. 733; 172 P.3d 361; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3041



November 14, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at State v. Russell, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 764 (Wash., Aug. 5, 2008)
Review denied by State v. Russell, 164 Wn.2d 1020, 195 P.3d 89, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 896 (Wash., Sept. 5, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the trial court (Washington) of second degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not violate defendant's constitutional right to public trial when it prohibited the media from photographing juvenile witnesses without consent because there was no closure of the courtroom. The trial court's prohibition on photographing minor witnesses without consent could not have even been considered akin to a partial closure. The trial court did not prohibit the media from recording the juvenile witnesses' testimony so long as they did not point the camera at the juvenile witnesses. Also, the record clearly showed that the trial court complied with the Wash. Gen. R. 16 requirements. The trial court made particularized findings to support its decision to limit photographing juvenile witnesses, repeatedly stating that it was concerned with cameras hindering the juvenile witnesses' ability to testify. Furthermore, the trial court repeatedly indicated that the ruling would not infringe on the ability of the public to be aware of the courtroom proceedings, and the trial court supported the limitation on photographing the juvenile witnesses on the specific circumstances of the case.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Drum


No. 35326-1-II Consolidated with 35840-9-II and 36438-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3044



November 14, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Drum, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3080 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 14, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington superior court dismissed as untimely defendant's July 2006 Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8 motion challenging his May 2005 amended judgment and sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the superior court's dismissal of his July 2006 Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8 motion as untimely and his May 2005 resentencing on additional grounds he failed to include in his July Rule 7.8 motion. The appellate court found that the trial court's dismissal of defendant's motion was untimely where defendant's arguments were without merit. Because defendant's arguments lacked merit, he could not show that any of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100's exceptions applied to relieve him from the one-year time bar. The appellate court could not reach new issues relating to defendant's amended judgment and sentence. Wash. R. App. P. 2.4(b) did not apply to bring defendant's May 2005 amended judgment and sentence before the appellate court. Defendant's May 2005 amended judgment and sentence became final when the sentencing court filed it on May 27, 2005. Defendant failed to show that his personal restraint petition (PRP) arguments were not time barred. His December 2006 PRP was untimely as defendant failed to show that if fell within the Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100(6) exception to the one-year time bar. Defendant's June 2007 PRP was time barred.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1467 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nguyen


No. 57942-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3025



November 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Nguyen, 141 Wn. App. 1026, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3053 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a Washington superior court, defendant was convicted of first-degree felony murder. After exhausting his direct appeals, defendant filed motions under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8 to vacate his conviction. The trial court denied the motions, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred by excluding him from a chambers conference concerning a potential conflict of interest arising from defense counsel's representation of a potential State's witness. However, the appellate court held that: (1) the potential conflict of interest was a legal matter in which defendant's opinion was not relevant, (2) the hearing concerned confidential information about the potential witness that defendant had no right to know, (3) the hearing was thus not a critical stage of the criminal proceedings at which defendant had a Sixth Amendment right to be present, and (4) closure of the courtroom for the hearing did not violate his right to a public trial under the Sixth Amendment or Wash. Const. art. I, § 22, or the public's right to open justice under Wash. Const. art. I, § 10. Defendant's right to conflict-free counsel was not violated because the State neither called nor interviewed the proposed witness, and defendant did not show that the trial court erred by declining to unseal the chambers conference record or by failing to appoint counsel for his motions. Various additional pro se claims asserted by defendant were without merit.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of the motions for relief from judgment was affirmed.

State v. Everybodytalksabout


No. 59147-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3024



November 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Everybodytalksabout, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3074 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 13, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court convicted defendant, pursuant to a guilty plea, of first degree manslaughter. The court imposed a standard range sentence and a mandatory $500 victim penalty assessment (VPA). The court also signed the agreed restitution. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in requiring him to pay the VPA and restitution because the victim was killed while attempting to commit a felony. The appellate court found that even assuming the victim's survivors may not have qualified for benefits under Wash. Rev. Code § 7.68.070 because he was killed while attempting to commit a crime, this did not eliminate the court's authority under Wash. Rev. Code § 7.68.035 to require defendant to pay the VPA. The VPA was paid into a fund. Under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.753(5), the trial court had the authority to order restitution because defendant pleaded guilty to fatally injuring the victim. The statute did not require that the victim be "innocent." Defendant agreed to pay restitution in full to the victim on charged counts in his plea agreement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Parentage of M.F.


No. 58658-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


141 Wn. App. 558; 170 P.3d 601; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2968



November 5, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by In re Parentage of Frazier, 163 Wn.2d 1052, 187 P.3d 752, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 698 (2008)
Related proceeding at In re Marriage of Corbin, 146 Wn. App. 1023, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 2084 (2008)
Affirmed by Parentage of M.F. John Corbin v. Reiman, 2010 Wash. LEXIS 262 (Wash., Apr. 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: Snohomish. Superior Court Cause No: 06-3-00974-8.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the mother, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which found in favor of respondent, the former stepfather (stepfather), and denied the mother's motion to dismiss the stepfather's petition seeking residential time with the child. The stepfather was also made a de facto parent and a guardian ad litem was appointed for the child; the mother's motion to revise the orders was denied.


OVERVIEW: The primary issue in the case was whether the stepfather had a cause of action as a de facto parent for residential time with his former stepdaughter. The appellate court held that he did not. The superior court denied the mother's motion to dismiss the petition under Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 12(b)(6) and also entered a temporary order making a threshold determination that the stepfather was a de facto parent and ordered a reunification process between him and his former stepdaughter. The other order appointed a guardian ad litem for the child and directed further actions. The mother's motion to revise those two orders was denied and the appellate court granted discretionary review. The appellate court held that the existing parenting plan governing residential time with the child could not be modified without the statutorily required showing of adequate cause, and that no good cause was shown. Failure to apply the modification requirements of Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.260 constituted an abuse of discretion. The trial court's statement of what constituted a prima facie case for de facto parenthood omitted reference to necessary factors. Accordingly, it was incorrect.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order denying the mother's motion to dismiss, the order on revision, and the two underlying orders. The stepfather's petition seeking visitation was dismissed.

 

1470 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Det. of Keeney


No. 25277-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


141 Wn. App. 318; 169 P.3d 852; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2888



October 23, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT WALLA WALLA COUNTY. Superior Court No: 04-2-00752-7. Date filed in Superior Court: 5/5/06. Superior Court Judge signing: ROBERT L. ZAGELOW.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury determined that appellant was a sexually violent predator (SVP) and he was civilly committed by the Superior Court of Walla Walla County (Washington). Appellant challenged his commitment, asserting that the SVP statute was unconstitutionally vague, that his right to a unanimous jury verdict was violated, and that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to entertain the commitment hearing because he was unlawfully imprisoned at the time.


OVERVIEW: While there may be a degree of uncertainty in predictions of future violence under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.020(7), the uncertainty did not rise to the level of unconstitutional vagueness. Moreover, any lack of definiteness was mitigated by other procedural protections that were attendant to SVP hearings, as well as the State's burden of proof beyond a reasonable doubt. Fact finders were not required to consider any particular time frame when making the determination. Therefore, the phrase, "likely to engage in predatory acts of sexual violence," was not unconstitutionally vague. Also, appellant's right to a unanimous jury verdict was not violated. Finally, "lawful custody" was not a jurisdictional prerequisite to a valid petition for civil commitment as a SVP. The question of the lawfulness of an individual's detention was a separate question, involving separate proceedings, and was not included in the inquiry as to whether an individual met the criteria for civil commitment as a SVP.


OUTCOME: Appellant's commitment was affirmed.

State v. McCormick


No. 58255-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


141 Wn. App. 256; 169 P.3d 508; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2865



October 22, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. McCormick, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3303 (Wash. Ct. App., Dec. 24, 2007)
Review granted by State v. McCormick, 164 Wn.2d 1002, 190 P.3d 55, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 768 (2008)
Affirmed by State v. McCormick, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 730 (Wash., Aug. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: Snohomish. Superior Court Cause No: 99-1-01667-4. Date filed in Superior Court: May 16, 2006 -- Order of Commitment. May 17, 2006 -- Order Modifying Judgment. May 17, 2006 -- Order Vacating SSOSA. Superior Court Judge Signing: Thomas J. Wynne.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court County: Snohomish Superior Court (Washington) an order revoking his special sexual offender sentencing alternative (SSOSA) after finding that defendant violated the conditions of his suspended sentence for first degree rape of a child by frequenting a place where minors were known to congregate, and by failing to complete a sexual deviancy treatment program.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State had to prove that his violation was willful. The court followed the clear precedent of the decision in State v. Gropper and held that no finding of willfulness was required. According to Gropper, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.200(2)(c), recodified as Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.634, did not require a court to consider willfulness before ordering incarceration for a violation of a condition that did not involve a financial obligation. By its terms, that section of the statute applied to orders regarding payment of legal financial obligations and community service obligations. Nothing in the statute suggested that subsection (2)(c) should be applied to any other type of violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

 

1472 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Aguilar-Torres


No. 35896-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2840



October 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Aguilar-Torres, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2856 (Wash. Ct. App., Oct. 16, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a Washington trial court, defendant was convicted of first-degree child molestation. Besides imposing prison sentences, the trial court imposed lifetime community custody with various crime-related prohibitions and affirmative conditions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The conditions imposed on defendant included: (1) requiring him to take an alcohol-dependency drug if his community corrections officer so directed; (2) prohibiting possession of alcohol; (3) prohibiting visiting places where alcoholic beverages were the primary sale item; (4) prohibiting possession of drug paraphernalia; and (5) prohibiting the possession of deadly weapons. The appellate court noted that although a trial court was authorized under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.505(8) to impose crime-related prohibitions and affirmative conditions when a defendant committed certain crimes, including first-degree child molestation, conditions that did not reasonably relate to the circumstances of the crime were unlawful unless explicitly permitted by statute. None of the first three conditions had been shown to be reasonably related to defendant's crime. Thus, unless the State came forward on remand with evidence connecting the crime with the first three conditions, the trial court would have to strike those conditions. The trial court was also directed to strike the last two conditions as not authorized by statute.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

State v. C.C.


No. 34046-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2843



October 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. C.C., 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2853 (Wash. Ct. App., Oct. 16, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile, sought review of the decision of the Pierce County Juvenile Court (Washington), which found him guilty of molesting five of his young female family members.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of molesting five of his young female family members; on appeal the court affirmed. A nurse's testimony was admitted under both Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.120 and Wash. R. Evid. 803(a)(4) and appellant did not challenge the admission of the statement under Wash. R. Evid. 803(a)(4). Thus, it was assumed that the trial court properly admitted the child's statement to the nurse under R. 803(a)(4) and did not address the admissibility of victim one's statements to the nurse under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.120. The evidence was sufficient to support a conviction for first-degree child molestation pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.083 because victim one told a forensic child interviewer that appellant approached her, pulled her pants down, and touched her buttocks. His conviction for indecent liberties was appropriate because there was sufficient evidence showing that, at different times, appellant pulled down victim one's and victim five's pants and touched their bare buttocks. His conviction for indecent exposure was proper because there was evidence supporting the finding that appellant knew that his actions would cause reasonable affront or alarm.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1474 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. L.B.-M. v. McLemore


NO. 59433-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2833



October 15, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State ex rel. L.B.-M. v. McLemore, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2852 (Wash. Ct. App., Oct. 15, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother's child resided with appellant, the child's aunt, until the mother petitioned to modify the parenting plan. Although the mother's petition did not meet the standards necessary for modification under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.260, the Washington trial court found that the language in the parenting plan created an alternate modification process. The aunt appealed the modification order.


OVERVIEW: Because the parenting plan referred to modification upon a noncustodial parent's successful completion of a drug treatment program - which was a situation that would not support a modification petition under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.260 because it was not a substantial change in the circumstances of either the child or the aunt - that reference demonstrated that the parties and the trial court contemplated that modification could take place without meeting the requirements of Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.260. Furthermore, the child's safety and welfare were still protected by the parenting plan criteria set forth in Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.187, even if Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.260 was not applied. Thus, because the aunt failed to foster the bond that the mother was developing with the child and the trial court's uncontested conclusion that modification was in the child's best interest, the trial court's modification order was consistent with Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.187. Therefore, the trial court's modification order was proper because the parties agreed to a modification procedure alternative to the modification statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.260.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1475 of 2278 DOCUMENTS




Abbey Rd. Group, LLC v. City of Bonney Lake


No. 35383-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


141 Wn. App. 184; 167 P.3d 1213; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2794



October 9, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Abbey Rd. Group, LLC v. City of Bonney Lake, 163 Wn.2d 1045, 187 P.3d 750, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 661 (2008)
Affirmed by Abbey Rd. Group. LLC v. City of Bonney Lake, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 966 (Wash., Oct. 8, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city appealed a decision by a Washington superior court, which reversed a hearing examiner's decision denying vested development rights to respondent developer for a 575-unit condominium project within the city.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that development rights did not vest because the developer failed to file a building permit application before the city adopted new zoning and permit standards applicable to the developer's property. Wash. Rev. Code § 19.27.095(1) required the developer to submit a valid and fully complete building permit application for development rights to vest on the date of the application. Because the developer did not submit a building permit application, it failed to show that the hearing examiner erroneously interpreted Washington's vested rights doctrine or erroneously applied the law to the facts. No development rights vested when the developer filed an application for site development plan review. The city's development scheme was not so burdensome that it unconstitutionally frustrated vesting rights under ordinances and building codes in effect when a building permit was filed, nor did it conflict with statutory or case law controlling vesting of development rights. Accordingly, the court was not persuaded that the hearing examiner erroneously interpreted or applied the law or that the hearing examiner's decision was clearly erroneous or constitutionally flawed.


OUTCOME: The superior court's decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.


 

1476 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Rudolph


No. 32658-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


141 Wn. App. 59; 168 P.3d 430; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2749



October 2, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at State v. Rudolph, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 596 (Wash., June 4, 2008)
Review denied by State v. Rudolph, 163 Wn.2d 1045, 190 P.3d 54, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 609 (Wash., June 25, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [**1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree robbery. The Washington trial court sentenced him to life-without-parole under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA), Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.570, based on his prior out-of-state felony convictions. Defendant challenged the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the POAA sentencing procedures were unconstitutional because they allowed the trial court to make factual findings about prior convictions, rather than requiring a jury to make those findings. The appellate court held that under the Almendarez-Torres, Apprendi, and Blakely rules, the POAA was a constitutionally permissible statute because it was a recidivism statute. A life sentence under the POAA depended only on the fact of prior convictions. Case law did not require a jury to decide the identity of the prior perpetrator, which was intrinsic to the clearly excepted fact of a prior conviction itself, given the case law's continued adherence to excepting the fact of prior conviction from the jury trial requirement. Therefore, defendant had no right to a jury trial on the issue of whether he was the person who committed previous strike offenses that subjected him to a POAA sentence of life without parole. Accordingly, the trial court properly entered findings about defendant's prior convictions, including his identity as the perpetrator.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

Gaines v. Employment Sec. Dep't


No. 58664-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


140 Wn. App. 791; 166 P.3d 1257; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2636



September 17, 2007, Filed  
September 17, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 05-2-37351-2 SEA. Date filed in Superior Court: October 21, 2005; July 21, 2006. Superior Court Judge Signing: The Honorable Linda Lau.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public employee lost her job and was granted a year of commissioner approved training (CAT). When she quit a job while attending CAT, respondent Washington Department of Employment Security denied the benefits she already was receiving. An administrative law judge (ALJ) overturned the Department's holding, the commissioner rejected the ALJ's decision, and the Superior Court of King County, Washington, affirmed. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the employee challenged the commissioner's reversal of the ALJ's determination that she was not disqualified from receiving benefits pursuant to former Wash. Rev. Code § 50.20.100 and Wash. Rev. Code § 50.20.080 as she was not obligated to accept suitable positions while in CAT. The appellate court found that the commissioner's decision provided no authority for his determination that once the employee undertook work, she could quit only for good cause. The commissioner erred in concluding that he was not required to consider the suitability of the work under former Wash. Rev. Code § 50.20.100. The ALJ was correct in concluding that the employee's leaving work after 11 days more properly constituted a refusal to work as allowed under the training provisions. This refusal did not disqualify the employee from receiving benefits. It was because the employee showed that the work was unsuitable that the ALJ correctly found she could refuse the work. Contrary to the commissioner's argument that the ALJ did not make any findings as to the suitability of the job, the ALJ specifically concluded the part-time job was unsuitable.


OUTCOME: The commissioner's decision was reversed and the decision of the ALJ was reinstated.

State v. Kinsey

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant entered guilty pleas to charges of attempting to elude and vehicular assault, the superior court (Washington) and imposed exceptional sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sentence, which took the form of consecutive standard range sentences, was based on the superior court's finding that the multiple offense policy resulted in a presumptive sentence that was clearly too lenient. OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for resentencing.
