Leskovar v. Nickels


No. 54354-7-I, (Consolidated with No. 54450-1-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


140 Wn. App. 770; 166 P.3d 1251; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2643



September 17, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Leskovar v. Nickels, 163 Wn.2d 1043, 187 P.3d 270, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 528 (Wash., June 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 04-2-05955-1.SEA -- Leskovar; 04-2-05857-1.SEA -- Atchison. Date filed in Superior Court: May 19, 2007. Superior Court Judge Signing: Bruce Hilyer.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's order granting the city's motion to dismiss was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens brought suit against respondents, a city and its mayor, seeking declaratory, injunctive, and other relief on the basis that the mayor's executive order granting employee benefits to city employees in same-sex marriages was invalid. The Superior Court of King County, Washington, granted the city's motion to dismiss. The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the citizens argued that the mayor's executive order granting employee benefits to city employees in same-sex marriages redefined marriage and violated Wash. Rev. Code § 26.04.010 and Wash. Rev. Code § 26.04.020 of Washington's Defense of Marriage Act. The appellate court disagreed, holding that the order neither conflicted with these statutes nor otherwise invaded a field preempted by a state statute; the citizens failed to show the state had preempted the field of employee benefits for the city. To the contrary, that field remained a matter of local concern in which the city exercised broad discretion. Wash. Rev. Code § 41.04.180 gave the city authority to provide benefits to employees and their dependents. Thus, the mayor was fully within his right to issue an executive order directing the provision of employee benefits to employees of the city. Moreover, the executive order extending benefits to city employees in same-sex marriages in the same manner as other city employees determined who was eligible for employee benefits. Nowhere did the order purport to give legal effect to same-sex marriages. And there was nothing in the order that conflicted with the Act.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order granting the city's motion to dismiss was affirmed.

Galvis v. Dep't of Transp.


No. 34604-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


140 Wn. App. 693; 167 P.3d 584; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2609



September 11, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Galvis v. Dep't of Transp., 163 Wn.2d 1041, 187 P.3d 269, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 548 (Wash., June 4, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Washington Department of Transportation (DOT), challenged an order from a trial court (Washington), which awarded just compensation and attorney fees to plaintiff property owners in an inverse condemnation action. The owners challenged an order awarding partial summary judgment to the DOT and holding that the Washington Highway Access Management Act (HAMA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 47.50, did not violate Wash. Const. art. I, § 16.


OVERVIEW: The DOT proposed a safety improvement project along part of a highway. The owners had access connections to the highway that the DOT intended to modify. After the DOT's proposal was upheld in administrative proceedings, the owners brought an action against the DOT, claiming that the HAMA facially violated Wash. Const. art. I, § 16 by allowing local governments to take property rights without just compensation. The trial court granted the DOT's partial summary judgment motion, ruling that Wash. Rev. Code ch. 47.50 did not violate the state constitution. On appeal, the court found that the trial court properly determined that the HAMA did not facially violate Wash. Const. art. I, § 16. Because the owners did not have a right to park in the public right of way, the elimination of on-street parking did not give rise to a takings claim. Because the privilege to park in the public right of way was not a compensable property right, it was not part of the "reasonable access" guaranteed by the Washington Constitution and the HAMA. Because the owners would have reasonable access to their properties, the trial court erred in awarding them just compensation and attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of partial summary judgment to the DOT. The court reversed the award of just compensation and attorney fees to the owners. The court denied the owners' request for appellate attorney fees.

 

1481 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


In re Custody of Z.


No. 33954-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2616



September 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals December 18, 2007. RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Custody of Z., 140 Wn. App. 1026, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2632 (Wash. Ct. App., Sept. 11, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prospective adoptive parents challenged a judgment of the Pierce County Superior Court (Washington) denying their third-party custody petition under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.10.030(1) and ordering the parties to establish an appropriate schedule to transfer physical custody of the child to the father.


OVERVIEW: The child's mother gave him to the adoptive parents, her brother and his wife, after his birth to adopt and raise. When the child was three months old, his father filed a paternity action. Eleven months later, the adoptive parents filed a third-party custody petition. The superior court found that the father was not unfit and ordered the adoptive parents to transfer the child to him. On appeal, the court held that substantial evidence supported the decision that the father was not unfit and that placing the child with him would not result in an actual detriment to the child's growth and development. There was no evidence establishing that the father was unfit or incapable of caring for the child, as the adoptive parents did not support their allegation that he used drugs with any evidence, and although the child's mother alleged that the father raped and the child was the result of that rape, the father was never charged with rape, a restraining order was not granted due to lack of evidence, and the guardian ad litem did not find the rape allegation credible enough to give it much weight. The superior court did not err when it applied the detriment to the child test.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the adoptive parents' petition was affirmed, the order staying the transfer of custody to the father was lifted, and the case was remanded to the superior court for entry of a schedule that would transfer physical custody to the father.

In re Pers. Restraint of Wheeler


No. 25480-1-III, (consolidated with, No. 25481-0-III)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


140 Wn. App. 670; 166 P.3d 871; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2617



September 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals October 23, 2007.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended by In re Pers. Restraint of Wheeler, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2876 (Wash. Ct. App., Oct. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT YAKIMA COUNTY. Superior Court No: 04-1-00327-5 (# 25480-1-III); 04-1-01130-8 (# 25481-0-III). Date filed in Superior Court: 7/7/04. Superior Court Judge signing: RUTH E. REUKAUF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, petitioner, pled guilty to first degree possession of stolen property, second degree malicious mischief and second degree theft. Respondent, Washington Department of Corrections (DOC), determined that the petitioner was ineligible for 50 percent earned early release credit. The Superior Court of Yakima County, Washington, imposed sentence and the petitioner filed a personal restraint petition.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced the petitioner to incarceration for 57 months on the possession of stolen property conviction and 29 months on the malicious mischief and second degree theft convictions, sentences to run concurrently. The DOC's initial risk assessment placed the petitioner in risk category RM-C, making him eligible for 50 percent earned early release under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.728. Subsequent risk assessments conducted however, placed the petitioner in risk category RM-B, rendering him ineligible. The appellate court ruled that the petitioner's due process rights were violated because he was not given notice or an opportunity to challenge the DOC's decision to change his risk assessment category to make him ineligible for 50 percent earned early release. There was nothing in the limited record before the appellate court to indicate that the petitioner was given notice of the reasons behind the DOC's decision to change his classification from RM-C to RM-B, making him ineligible for 50 percent earned early release, or that he had an opportunity to challenge the facts relied upon by the DOC to reach its decision.


OUTCOME: The petitioner's personal restraint petition was granted.

 

1483 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Lewis


No. 34014-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


141 Wn. App. 367; 166 P.3d 786; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2548



August 28, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Lewis, 163 Wn.2d 1030, 185 P.3d 1195, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 381 (Wash., Apr. 30, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a Washington trial court of second degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erroneously found him competent to stand trial because no developmental disability expert had tested him. The court of appeals disagreed. No one, including defense counsel and defendant himself, advised the trial court of any concerns that defendant might have developmental disabilities. Moreover, during defendant's initial evaluation, none of the examining professionals noticed any reason to find defendant developmentally disabled. Wash. Rev. Code § 10.77.090(1)(c) did not specify who must perform the developmental disability evaluation or how the evaluation should have been conducted. Nor did § 10.77.090(1)(c) require the trial court to make a specific finding about the presence or absence of a developmental disability in connection with determining defendant's competency to stand trial. Furthermore, none of the three experts, not even defendant's, opined that defendant was developmentally disabled. Although no one performed a formal IQ test, all three experts placed defendant's IQ above 70 and, thus, outside the IQ range for mental retardation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1484 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stickel


No. 58137-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2531



August 27, 2007 


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Stickel, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2580 (Wash. Ct. App., Aug. 27, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree child rape and two counts of first degree child molestation for the rape of his daughter. The Washington trial court sentenced defendant under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.712 to a high-end minimum term, and sentenced defendant to community custody for life following release from confinement and imposed a variety of conditions, some statutory, some discretionary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: There was no evidence in the record that alcohol or drugs contributed to the crimes committed by defendant. The State asserted that it was reasonable to impose these conditions to enhance community safety by preventing the perpetrator from purchasing or possessing alcohol and to submit to substance abuse treatment or counseling. The appellate court found that these assertions were not supported by the evidence. The allegations of alcohol and drug use were not shown to have contributed to the crimes committed and therefore the imposition of these conditions exceeded the sentencing court's authority. Also, the condition requiring the affirmative conduct or treatment for substance abuse must be stricken, and there was no evidence in the case that the Internet contributed to defendant's offenses. Furthermore, the appellate court rejected defendant's claim that the condition prohibiting possession of pornography was overbroad. Defendant could not show that the pornography prohibition was impermissibly vague in all applications because there were some materials that any reasonable person would understand to constitute pornography. On its face, the proscription was not ambiguous.


OUTCOME: The conditions imposed regarding substance abuse treatment, the purchase or possession of alcohol (not alcohol consumption), and access to the Internet were reversed and the case remanded to strike those conditions, and the judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Utter v. Dep't of Soc. & Health Servs.


No. 35399-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


140 Wn. App. 293; 165 P.3d 399; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2495



August 21, 2007, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Washington, Department of Social and Health Services, challenged a superior court (Washington) ruling that invalidated the Department's claim for reimbursement from appellee accused for costs relating to his competency evaluation and treatment pending criminal charges.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court found the accused to be incompetent to stand trial, the State dismissed its information, and the accused was not convicted. Nevertheless, an administrative law judge (ALJ) granted the Department's claim for reimbursement. On appeal, the court reconciled the potentially conflicting provisions of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.01.160, Wash. Rev. Code § 10.77.250, and Wash. Rev. Code § 43.20B.330 and concluded that the costs relating to the accused's competency evaluation and treatment were expenses specially incurred by the State in prosecuting him. As such, for the Department to recover those costs, if at all, it had to seek reimbursement under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.01.160, not Wash. Rev. Code § 10.77.250 and Wash. Rev. Code § 43.20B.330, but because the accused was never a convicted defendant, the Department had no statutory authority under § 10.01.160 to require him to pay the costs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ALJ's decision and remanded to the Department to set aside the ALJ's final order.

 

1486 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Glenn


No. 34790-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2501



August 21, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Glenn, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2519 (Wash. Ct. App., Aug. 21, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted before the trial court (Washington) of three counts of vehicular assault and one count of bail jumping. Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: At sentencing, the State argued that defendant's three prior misdemeanors did not wash out defendant's offender score under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.525(2), because defendant had been convicted of two misdemeanor offenses in 1996, and one misdemeanor offense in 2001, and was, therefore, not conviction-free for the required five-year period. On appeal, defendant argued that his offender scores were incorrect. The primary issue was whether the trial court erred by considering three misdemeanor offenses that interrupted the five-year wash-out period when the State's proof of the misdemeanor offenses was silent as to whether defendant was represented by counsel. Nevertheless, defendant's prior misdemeanor convictions were facially valid. Defendant did not attempt to challenge their validity prior to sentencing. Defendant's argument that the trial court had to presume constitutional invalidity because the State's proof did not affirmatively demonstrate constitutional validity had no merit. The State was entitled to rely on the proof of a defendant's prior conviction at sentencing until the prior conviction was corrected or vacated or unless the conviction was facially invalid.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In re Interest of S.H.


No. 24781-3-III (consolidated with No. 24782-1-III, No. 24783-0-III, No. 24795-3-III, No. 24796-1-III, No. 24797-0-III)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2456



August 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Interest of S.H., 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2466 (Wash. Ct. App., Aug. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Superior Court County: OKANOGAN. Docket No(s): 05-7-00018-0, 05-7-00019-8, 05-7-00020-1. Judge signing: JACK G. BURCHARD. Date filed: NOVEMBER 15, 2005.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the parents, sought review of the decision Superior Court of Okanogan County (Washington), which found in favor of respondent, the Department of Social and Health Services (Department), and terminated the parents' parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The parents appealed the trial court's termination of their parental rights, but the appellate court affirmed. Although the no-contact order was entered in a cause completely independent and separate from the termination case, under Wash. R. Evid. 201 the trial court was permitted to take judicial notice of a fact not subject to reasonable dispute and capable of accurate and ready determination by resort to sources whose accuracy could not have been reasonably questioned. Both parents testified at trial as to the existence of the no-contact order. The only issue concerned the dates that order was in effect. That was capable of accurate and ready determination via the court system database. Thus, the trial court did not err by taking judicial notice of the terms of the no-contact order. Additionally, Wash. Rev. Code §§ 13.34.180 and 13.34.190 were constitutional. The mother was offered adequate services by the Department and there was evidence to support the finding under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.180(1)(e) that there was little likelihood that conditions would be remedied so that the children could return to her in the near future.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1488 of 2278 DOCUMENTS




Post v. City of Tacoma


No. 34808-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


140 Wn. App. 155; 165 P.3d 37; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2434



August 14, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Released for Publication on August 14, 2007.
Review granted by Post v. City of Tacoma, 163 Wn.2d 1038, 187 P.3d 268, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 501 (2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by Post v. City of Tacoma, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 970 (Wash., Oct. 15, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sued respondents, a city, a collection agency, and others, claiming that the fines imposed under the city's building and structures code were excessive, unconstitutional, and outside the city's statutory authority. The Washington trial court granted summary judgment to the city. The owner challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The procedural requirement of the Land Use Petition Act (LUPA) applied as the imposition of fines to enforce city ordinances was a land use decision under Wash. Rev Code. § 36.70C.020(1)(c). The notice of violation and penalties were final determinations under Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C.020(1) as the hearing officer had the highest level of authority to make determinations and thus, his decisions were final. The owner's argument that the city was required to enforce the ordinance in a court of limited jurisdiction was not considered where he had offered no legal authority for the argument. Even if it were considered, the argument lacked merit as the owner had raised claims based on the state and federal constitutions. Under case law, those claims were subject to superior court jurisdiction. The owner's initial request for monetary damages did not bar LUPA's application as the trial court had dismissed all damage claims. Thus, the only claims relevant to the trial court's order and the appeal were for declaratory and injunctive relief. Since the owner had not filed a land use petition or exhausted his administrative remedies, his claims were barred by LUPA.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment to the city was affirmed.


 

1489 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Fleming


No. 32499-7-II / 33798-3-IINo. 32499-7-II / 33798-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


140 Wn. App. 132; 170 P.3d 50; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2439



August 14, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: OPINION PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Fleming, 163 Wn.2d 1047, 187 P.3d 750, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 719 (Wash., July 8, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Washington trial court found defendant guilty of witness tampering. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under Wash. Const. art. I, § 21, defendant argued that he was denied his constitutional right to a unanimous verdict, which could include the right to jury unanimity as to the means by which he committed the crime. The State presented substantial evidence only that defendant tried to induce the victim to absent himself from the proceedings. The only evidence indicating a different means of tampering was the conversation where his grandmother asked the victim to change his story, but that conversation illustrated only her crime, not defendant's. Although the evidence was insufficient evidence to establish that defendant sought to induce the victim to testify falsely or unlawfully withhold testimony, defendant's conviction for witness tampering was based on an alternative means of committing the offense - inducing the victim to disappear. Also, substantial evidence supported that alternative. Thus, defendant was not denied his right to jury unanimity. Also, the standard sentence range was the same whether defendant's offender score was nine or 11. Thus, the trial court's failure to specifically address whether some prior convictions constituted same criminal conduct was harmless.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Donahue v. Cent. Wash. Univ.


No. 24891-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


140 Wn. App. 17; 163 P.3d 801; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2339



August 7, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT KITTITAS. Superior Court No: 02-2-00307-1. Date filed in Superior Court: FEBRUARY 7, 2005. Superior Court Judge signing: MICHAEL E. COOPER.



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant professor filed an administrative grievance against respondent public university, challenging his reassignment and seeking reinstatement and damages. A hearing officer denied relief. The university's board issued a final order adopting the officer's findings and conclusions. The professor unsuccessfully appealed to a Washington superior court and sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The professor contended that he had been improperly reassigned from the computer sciences department to teach humanities after having filed two grievances. Reviewing the board's order under the Washington Administrative Procedure Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 34.05.570, the court rejected the professor's claims, holding that: (1) the board's decision was not arbitrary or capricious because it was not taken without regard to the facts and circumstances presented; (2) the order did not fail to follow the proscribed procedure of the university's faculty code; (3) the reassignment was not a retaliation for the two earlier grievances because the professor did not lose tenure, was not demoted, and did not receive a reduction in pay, and the university justified its actions based on university need and the professor's past performance; (4) the professor was not denied due process because he was not deprived of any property right and he received proper notification and hearing; and (5) the professor's free speech rights were not violated because he did not demonstrate that his speech was a substantial or motivating factor in the reassignment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the board's order.

Tharaldson v. T & T Trucking, Inc.


No. 35052-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2352



August 7, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Tharaldson v. T&T Trucking, Inc., 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2442 (Wash. Ct. App., Aug. 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from Pierce County Superior Court, 05-2-11626-4; Honorable Kathryn J Nelson. Judgment Date: 06/02/2006.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a workers' compensation action, appellant, the Washington Department of Labor and Industries, sought review of an order from the Pierce County Superior Court (Washington), which awarded summary judgment to respondent employee and vacated the Department's order demanding $ 13,908 from the employee's settlement with a third-party tortfeasor. The employee requested attorney fees under Wash. Rev. Code § 51.52.130.


OVERVIEW: The employee injured his back at work. While he was receiving treatment for the back injury, he was involved in a motor vehicle collision, unrelated to his employment. He sued the driver who caused the vehicle accident. The employee settled the lawsuit. The Department demanded that the employee pay reimbursement. The Washington Board of Industrial Insurance Appeals found that the Department had a right to reimbursement for payments attributable to the motor vehicle accident. The trial court, however, awarded summary judgment to the employee. On appeal, the court found that the evidence did not establish the reimbursement claim. The Department failed to provide substantial evidence that the third party was responsible for the benefits the employee received. Although two medical experts concluded that the car accident aggravated the employee's industrial injury, neither could say that he required additional treatment or recuperation as a consequence of the car accident. Thus, the Department did not show that the car accident caused it to make expenditures under Wash. Rev. Code § 51.24.060(1)(c). Absent such a showing, sufficient evidence did not support its reimbursement demand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court granted the employee's request for attorney fees.

 

1492 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


City of Bellevue v. O'Connell


No. 58197-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2305



August 6, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: City of Bellevue v. O'Connell, 139 Wn. App. 1096, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2381 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a Washington trial court, defendant was convicted of assault under former Bellevue, Wash., City Code § 10A.36.010 (repealed 2005). Defendant appealed his conviction, challenging the constitutionality of the assault ordinance as overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Bellevue, Wash., City Code § 10A.36.010 made unlawful "any act and word or threat" that intentionally placed another person in fear or apprehension of bodily injury. Subjecting the ordinance to overbreadth analysis under federal constitutional law, the court concluded that: (1) the ordinance proscribed protected speech because it did not prohibit only "true threats," that is, statements reasonably interpreted as a serious expression of intention to inflict bodily harm; but (2) the ordinance did not make unlawful a real and substantial amount of protected speech because it was directed against specific conduct, namely, acting with the intent to place a person in fear or apprehension of bodily injury; and (3) the ordinance could be saved by a sufficient limiting construction because its specific intent requirement allowed it to be construed as prohibiting only true threats. Thus, the ordinance was not overbroad.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1493 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


No. 34917-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2196



July 31, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Smith, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2332 (Wash. Ct. App., July 31, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court convicted defendant for attempted to elude a pursuing police vehicle. Defendant was sentenced to 10 months. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the jury instructions were erroneous, his counsel was ineffective, and the trial court failed to properly determine his criminal history. Defendant argued that the trial court erred by instructing the jury without defining the "reckless manner" standard of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.024(1) and instead instructed the jury using the "willful or wanton" standard of former § 46.61.024(1). The appellate court noted that "reckless" conduct was established by proof of "willful or wanton" conduct. The erroneous instruction was harmless error. The trial court did not err in giving instruction number 9 as the inferred fact of driving in a reckless manner flowed from the evidence or excessive speed. Although counsel failed to object to the erroneous instructions, because "reckless manner" was subsumed within the higher standard of "willful or wanton" conduct, a proper instruction would not have changed the trial's outcome. The trial court erred by relying on only the Statement of Prosecuting Attorney to determine defendant's criminal history and to calculate his offender score as it was insufficient and defendant's failure to object did not constitute an acknowledgement.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed; the judgment was remanded for recalculation of his sentence, allowing the State to prove his criminal history by a preponderance of the evidence.

State v. Roswell


NO. 34334-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2219



July 31, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Roswell, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2296 (Wash. Ct. App., July 31, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of a Washington trial court convicting him of two counts of communicating with a minor for immoral purposes in violation of Wash. Rev. Stat. § 9.68A.090(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for touching and asking the two victims, who were younger than 18 years old, to have sex with him. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions because: (1) the first victim testified that defendant began to talk about sex about a week after he began touching her; (2) the first victim told both the police and an interviewer at the sexual assault center that defendant asked her to have sex at least twice; (3) the second victim heard defendant ask the first victim for sex; and (4) the second victim testified that defendant well talked about sex with her and asked her to have sex with him on several occasions. Defendant waived his right to argue that the evidence was insufficient to support a finding that he was convicted of a felony sex offense prior to May 15, 2005 because he stipulated that he had a previous third-degree child molestation conviction. However, the court remanded to the case to correct defendant's sentence, because his total sentence of nine years and eight months in prison and 60 months of community custody exceeded the 10-year maximum sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed but the case was remanded for correction of his sentence so that it did not exceed the 10-year maximum sentence for class B felonies.

In re Det. of Strand


NO. 34442-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


139 Wn. App. 904; 162 P.3d 1195; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2181



July 31, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part In re Det. of Strand, 163 Wn.2d 1022, 185 P.3d 1195, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 414 (2008)
Affirmed by In re Det. of Strand, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 963 (Wash., Oct. 8, 2009)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a sexually violent predator (SVP) commitment petition and a certification for determination of probable cause under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.010 et seq. with respect to appellant sex offender. A Washington trial court jury determined that the sex offender was an SVP. The sex offender appealed his commitment.


OVERVIEW: The sex offender argued that he had been wrongly deprived of counsel during his pre-petition SVP evaluation. However, the appellate court held that he had no constitutional right to counsel during such an evaluation; also, his Fifth Amendment self-incrimination privilege had not been violated during the evaluation interview because he had not been compelled to answer any of the State's queries, and thus the interview was not an "interrogation" for Fifth Amendment purposes. The offender argued that his attorney provided ineffective assistance by failing to object to the evaluation procedure or dispute the voluntariness of his statements, but the appellate court noted that the offender had acquiesced in the procedure and signed a consent form. The offender requested a new trial because the trial court, due to a taping error, had not preserved a witness's testimony in a verbatim report. However, the appellate court noted that he had no due process right to such a report, there was no showing that the witness's deposition and a reconstructed narrative record would not have allowed effective appellate review, and the offender had made no attempt to supplement the record with affidavits.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the commitment.

Chandler v. Office of the Ins. Comm'r


No. 57853-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


141 Wn. App. 639; 173 P.3d 275; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2211



July 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: Order Granting Motion to Publish November 19, 2007.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Chandler v. State of Wash., Office of Ins. Comm'r, 139 Wn. App. 1081, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2269 (Wash. Ct. App., July 30, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an insurance agent, sought review of the decision of the Snohomish County Superior Court (Washington), which found in favor of respondent, the Office of the Insurance Commissioner, and affirmed the review judge's final order ruling that there was substantial evidence of the agent's untrustworthiness and that he was not qualified to be an insurance agent under Wash. Rev. Code § 48.17.530(1)(h).


OVERVIEW: The agent challenged the order revoking his Washington insurance agent's license, but the appellate court affirmed, stating that substantial evidence supported the review judge's decision under the statutory duty of care found in Wash. Rev. Code § 48.01.030. The agent had targeted senior citizens as his clientele and had represented himself as an elder planner. Lead cards sent out confused some customers who though that they were sent by the county assessor's office and the review judge's conclusion that the use of the cards was misleading and deceptive was supported by substantial evidence, including calls to the assessor's office and the attorney general. Additionally, his application had asked whether he had any complaints filed against him and the agent should have answered yes under Wash. Rev. Code § 48.17.090(3) since he had received a written notice of a complaint from the California Insurance Department to which he responded. The appellate court did not need to decide whether the review judge properly adopted a heightened standard of care because substantial evidence supported her decision under the statutory duty of care set forth in Wash. Rev. Code § 48.01.030.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the review judge's order revoking the agent's insurance license.

 

1497 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin


No. 58634-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2179



July 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Martin, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2286 (Wash. Ct. App., July 30, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court convicted defendant of second degree burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by refusing to instruct the jury on the lesser included offense of second degree criminal trespass. The appellate court found that the evidence sufficiently established that defendant entered the fenced area with the intent to take items from the dumpster without permission from the owner of the property. Defendant testified that he intended to take any item of interest to him that he found in the dumpster inside the fenced area. These items were presumed to have some value. The evidence did not support the inference that defendant committed the lesser included offense of second degree criminal trespass. Instruction 11 did not relieve the State of its burden of proving an essential element of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant did not object to Instruction 11 at trial. The objection to the instruction he raised on appeal was without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1498 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Post v. City of Tacoma


No. 34798-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2120



July 24, 2007, Fled


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Post v. City of Tacoma, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2250 (Wash. Ct. App., July 24, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant private property owners filed a class action complaint against respondent city to challenge the city's water disposal fees. A Washington trial court granted the city's motion for summary judgment and denied the property owners' cross-motion for declaratory relief. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under Wash. Rev. Code §§ 35.67.025 and 35.92.021, city property was subject to charges for storm water control facilities to the same extent as private persons and private property, but in setting these charges, consideration was allowed for "in-kind services." Accordingly, the city enacted an ordinance preventing the levying of storm water fees against city streets, having determined that those streets provided a benefit to storm water drainage equal to the charge that would otherwise be imposed on the city. The private property owners claimed that this exemption unconstitutionally burdened them and exceeded the city's statutory authority. However, the court held that the ordinance articulated a reasonable basis for excluding city streets from storm water charges; the declaration that city streets provided an in-kind service was neither arbitrary nor capricious nor in violation of the statute's plain language. The property owners offered no evidence, other than their own affidavit, to support the contention that the ordinance resulted in higher charges to them, and even if this contention were true, there was no showing that such an increase was either a tax or a fee.


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

 

1499 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. T.J.M.


No. 34809-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


139 Wn. App. 845; 162 P.3d 1175; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2123



July 24, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Manaois, 163 Wn.2d 1025, 185 P.3d 1194, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 396 (2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Washington juvenile court entered an adjudication finding appellant juvenile guilty of first degree rape of a child under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.073. Appellant challenged the juvenile court's judgment, arguing that Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.073 violated his constitutional rights to equal protection and substantive due process.


OVERVIEW: Because of the 11-year-old victim's sexual immaturity, appellant was able to manipulate the victim to perform sexual acts with him, even after the victim initially refused. By taking away a video game and promising its return if the victim cooperated, appellant persuaded the 11-year-old victim to engage in sexual intercourse to gratify his own sexual desires. Appellant's extra two years of age provided him with more sexual knowledge than the victim and some measure of power, which enabled him to obtain a younger, more acquiescent child for sexual experimentation - exactly the type of situation the legislature sought to prohibit with the strict age classifications in Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.073. Accordingly, the age classifications in § 9A.44.073 were not wholly unrelated to the State's legitimate interest in protecting immature children from sexual intercourse with persons more than two years older. Therefore, the statute did not violate appellant's equal protection rights and was constitutional. Also, due process did not require a fact-based inquiry into the 11-year-old victim's ability to consent to sexual intercourse with someone who was more than 24 months older.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the juvenile court's judgment.

 

1500 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Christophe


No. 58283-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2079



July 23, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Christophe, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2233 (Wash. Ct. App., July 23, 2007)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington superior court convicted defendant of one count of second degree assault with sexual motivation and one count of unlawful imprisonment. Defendant was sentenced to an indeterminate sentence on the assault count with a minimum term of 15 months of confinement and a maximum term of life, and 12 months confinement or the unlawful imprisonment count, to be served concurrently. Community custody was also imposed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that the community custody condition requiring him to abide by any additional conditions imposed by the department of corrections (DOC) exceeded the sentencing court's statutory authority; and the trial court erred in entering judgment and imposing sentence for unlawful imprisonment because it concluded that the two counts merged. The appellate court disagreed, holding first that unless and until the DOC imposed conditions beyond its authority, defendant's challenge to his community custody conditions was premature. The trial court also properly sentenced defendant on the unlawful imprisonment count, and there was no violation of double jeopardy in doing so. The compelled collection of DNA from defendant without a warrant pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754 was not unconstitutional as the state supreme court had recently upheld a similar complaint on the issue. Contrary to defendant's assertion, he was properly sentenced under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.712(1)(a)(ii) because he was convicted of assault in the second degree with a finding of sexual motivation, and Subsection (b) of that statute applied to prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Dependency of T.H.


NO. 58453-7-I, Linked with: 58575-4-I and 58799-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


139 Wn. App. 784; 162 P.3d 1141; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2106



July 23, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Dependency of Hackney, 162 Wn.2d 1001, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 959 (2007)
Subsequent appeal at In re Dependency of C.N., 142 Wn. App. 1013, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 3332 (Wash. Ct. App., Dec. 24, 2007)
Subsequent appeal at In re Dependency of T.S.S., 142 Wn. App. 1020, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 60 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 05-7-00738-7.KNT. Date filed in Superior Court: May 19, 2006. Superior Court Judge Signing: James A. Doerty.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found in favor of respondent, the Department of Social and Health Services (DSHS), and terminated the mother's parental rights to her son.


OVERVIEW: The mother appealed the termination of her parental rights to her son, primarily contending that because her visitation rights were limited, the DSHS did not meet its burden to show that it provided all services capable of correcting parental deficiencies. The appellate court concluded that although visitation was an important right of the family, it was not, on its own, a service that was required to be provided under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.180(1)(d). The district court properly restricted visitation under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.136(1)(b)(ii) in order to prevent harm to the child. And, the parenting deficiencies identified originally, including her lack of insight into how her behavior affected her child, were still present at the termination trial. Thus, the DSHS had established that the conditions of the parent-child relationship were not likely to be remedied in the near future.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1502 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thomas


No. 56540-1-I (Consolidated with No. 57285-7-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2099



July 23, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Thomas, 139 Wn. App. 1065, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2147 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with robbing two jewelry stores. A jury before the trial court (Washington) convicted defendant of attempted first degree robbery, first degree kidnapping, first degree assault, first degree robbery, and unlawful possession of a firearm. Six of the charges carried a firearm enhancement. Defendant was sentenced to 800 months' incarceration. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pointing a gun at a jewelry store's owner, defendant forced the owner to lie on the floor. Defendant then began to take jewelry. The owner broke free, and gunshots were exchanged. Defendant later entered a second store on false pretenses. Defendant eventually fled with jewelry. The State conceded that because attempted robbery was a class B felony, he should have received only a 36-month firearm enhancement on that charge. The evidence was sufficient to show that defendant was armed with a firearm in the second robbery, based on eyewitness testimony. Defendant's convictions for assault and robbery did not merge because proof of the assault was not necessary to prove first degree robbery. On the issue of whether jury instructions were properly given, the trial court did not err in defining kidnapping to the jury based on "restraint." The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for kidnapping. Before trial, defendant challenged fingerprint identification, claiming that the trial court did not analyzing his supporting material. The trial court correctly concluded that the accepted methodology for identifying people was through the use of fingerprints.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded for resentencing based on the issues properly conceded by the State. On all other issues, the appellate court affirmed.

 

1503 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barajas


No. 25055-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2031



July 19, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 04-1-01515 -8. Judge signing: VIC L. VANDERSCHOOR. Date filed: March 10, 2006.
State v. Barajas, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2127 (Wash. Ct. App., July 19, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part/Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a guilty plea to a second degree rape of a child charge in exchange for a special sex offender sentencing alternative (SSOSA) recommendation from the State. The SSOSA entered by the Superior Court for Benton County (Washington) contained numerous conditions of probation one of which prohibited defendant from perusing "any pornographic material." Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the community custody condition that prohibited the possession of "any pornographic material," claiming that the condition was unconstitutionally vague and had been held to have been unconstitutionally vague in State v. Sansone. The instant condition specifically provided: "Do not possess or peruse pornographic materials, including those found on the internet." After defendant served his sentence, he would be back on community supervision. He should not have to be placed in the risky position of waiting until he was arrested on a probation violation to discover what materials his CCO or the court considered pornographic. To avoid that hardship, and because the issue implicated defendant's due process rights, the appellate court addressed his challenge to the pornography prohibition. The prohibition was essentially identical to those found void for vagueness in other cases. As in those cases, once defendant was on probation, he would not know what conduct he had to avoid to protect against arbitrary enforcement. That lack of ascertainable standards violated due process.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court to provide a more specific definition of the prohibition consistent with defendant's treatment status and goals and a condition consistent with State v. Sansone. The trial court was otherwise affirmed.

 

1504 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Mendoza


NO. 34698-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


139 Wn. App. 693; 162 P.3d 439; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2003



July 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: OPINION PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Mendoza, 163 Wn.2d 1017, 180 P.3d 1292, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 279 (2008)
Affirmed by, Remanded by State v. Mendoza, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 435 (Wash., Apr. 16, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Washington trial court found defendant guilty of second degree robbery and unlawful imprisonment. The trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent terms of 84 months for second degree robbery and 60 months for unlawful imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed the 84-year-old victim and then demanded that the victim take him to a tavern. At sentencing, the State provided a statement of the prosecuting attorney that included a list of what the prosecutor believed was defendant's criminal history. Defendant did not object to the prosecutor's list. At sentencing, the State did not produce certified copies of any judgment or sentence showing defendant's alleged criminal history and failed to provide a reason for that omission. Also, the State relied solely on the argumentative statement of the prosecuting attorney concerning defendant's criminal history. No presentence report was submitted by the Washington Department of Corrections and the prosecutor's statement did not constitute a presentence report under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.500. Thus, the State failed to prove defendant's criminal history by a preponderance of the evidence or that defendant waived any challenge to the criminal history. Therefore, the trial court lacked the statutory authority to calculate defendant's offender score based on convictions the State failed to prove. Accordingly, defendant's sentence, based upon an incorrect offender score, was defective.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions, but remanded the case to the trial court for recalculation of his sentence based on his criminal record proven by a preponderance of the evidence, without limiting the State to the record at the prior sentencing hearing.

State v. Utanis


No. 34600-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1930



July 10, 2007, Decided


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Utanis, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1982 (Wash. Ct. App., July 10, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Pierce County Superior Court (Washington) of attempted first degree murder (domestic violence), a violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.32.030(1)(a), 9A.28.020, and 10.99.020, first degree burglary (domestic violence), a violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.52.020(l)(b) and 10.99.020, and of the aggravating circumstance that the offenses occurred within the sight or sound of the victim's minor children.


OVERVIEW: The court imposed a 25-year exceptional sentence. Defendant appealed claiming prosecutorial misconduct and that his exceptional sentence violated constitutional protections and had no statutory basis. Inter alia, defendant argued that the prosecutor committed misconduct in closing argument when she argued facts not in evidence to support her theory that he was obsessed with the victim and that that obsession fed his anger until he acted on it. The appellate court found no prejudicial misconduct. The record amply supported an inference that defendant was obsessed with the victim, could not understand or accept her rejection of him, and that that anger seethed in him until he broke into her house in the middle of the night and tried to choke her to death. Further, the court instructed the jury not to consider counsel's arguments as evidence, to disregard any statements the evidence did not support, and to follow the court's instructions. Further, defense counsel's failure to object to those statements would have served no legitimate tactical basis. In fact, defense counsel used the same argument to persuade the jury that defendant only intended to hurt the victim not kill her.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Matheson v. Gregoire


No. 35067-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


139 Wn. App. 624; 161 P.3d 486; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1937



July 10, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Matheson v. Gregoire, 163 Wn.2d 1020, 180 P.3d 1292, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 337 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Matheson v. Gregoire, 555 U.S. 881, 129 S. Ct. 197, 172 L. Ed. 2d 140, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 5552 (2008)
Related proceeding at Lanphere v. Wright, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 102756 (W.D. Wash., Oct. 29, 2009)
Related proceeding at Miller v. Wright, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 116533 (W.D. Wash., Oct. 6, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Thurston Superior Court. Docket No: 05-2-00892-7. Date filed: 06/09/2006. Judge signing: Honorable Richard A Strophy.
Matheson v. Liquor Control Bd., 132 Wn. App. 280, 130 P.3d 897, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 543 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retailer sued respondents, a tribe, the State of Washington, the Washington Department of Revenue (WDOR), and others, challenging the legality of a cigarette sales tax agreement. The Thurston Superior Court (Washington) dismissed the tribe as a defendant due to its sovereign immunity and dismissed the complaint for lack of an indispensable party. The retailer appealed. The tribe requested attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The tribe and the WDOR entered into an agreement regulating imposition of taxes on cigarette sales in Indian country. The retailer, a tribal member, sought injunctive relief, declaratory judgment, and damages. The appellate court determined that the trial court properly dismissed the tribe based on sovereign immunity because (1) the retailer sought equitable relief and damages, not just prospective relief, and (2) the tribe did not waive its sovereign immunity by entering into the agreement. The trial court did not err in finding that the tribe was an indispensable party, because, inter alia, (1) the tribe was necessary for just adjudication since a judgment rendered in the tribe's absence would greatly prejudice the tribe because the agreement would essentially disintegrate, (2) a remedy fashioned without the tribe would not be adequate to address the retailer's concerns, and (3) the tribal interest in immunity overcame the retailer's possible lack of an alternative remedy or forum. The tribe's request for attorney fees under Wash. R. App. P. 18.9(a) was denied because the retailer's appeal was not frivolous since he raised debatable issues on which reasonable minds would differ.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed. The appellate court declined to grant the tribe's request for attorney fees.

In re Postsentence Review of Smith


No. 58447-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


139 Wn. App. 600; 161 P.3d 483; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1911



July 9, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals July 13, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 04-1-14151-2.SEA. Superior Court Judge Signing: Laura C. Inveen.



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Washington Department of Corrections (DOC), challenged an order from the King County Superior Court (Washington), which sentenced respondent to six months of confinement and a community custody period for first-degree rape of a child.


OVERVIEW: Respondent pled guilty to first-degree rape of a child. The standard sentencing range was 93 to 163 months. Respondent had developmental delays. Respondent requested an exceptional sentence downward, and the State requested a sentence at the low end of the standard range. The trial court sentenced respondent to six months of confinement, an exceptional sentence below the standard range, but imposed a community custody period that was commensurate with the standard-range confinement period. The DOC petitioned that the case be remanded for resentencing. The court found that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535 authorized exceptional sentences. Further, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.545 specified that sentences of a year or less confinement could be followed by up to one year of community custody. Because community custody was authorized by statute, the trial court could impose a custody term shorter than the amount set by statute. The trial court imposed a sentence tailored to respondent's particular case. The sentence was consistent with Wash. Admin. Code § 437-20-010, which set community custody ranges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Townsend

COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE

State v. Townsend, 139 Wn. App. 1043, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1885 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Benton County Superior Court (Washington), which convicted her of first-degree theft, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.56.020(1)(a), and sentenced her to one year and one day in prison.

Tasker v. Dep't of Health


No. 35144-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1855



July 3, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tasker v. Dep't of Health, 139 Wn. App. 1041, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1881 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a provider of "electrodermal testing" (EDT), appealed a decision from the superior court (Washington), affirming the decision of appellee, the Department of Health (DOH), that she engaged in the unlicensed practice of medicine as defined by Wash. Rev. Code § 18.71.011 and of veterinary medicine as defined by Wash. Rev. Code § 18.92.010. Appellant was ordered to cease and desist and was issued a fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant used her EDT device to evaluate and identify medical illnesses or conditions through a client's "energy signature" and created a tincture based on the EDT readings and her evaluation. It was not error to conclude that she was engaged in the unlicensed practice of medicine and of veterinary medicine. The DOH was not required to demonstrate actual harm; Wash. Rev. Code § 18.120.010 did not apply. The EDT device was not used for biofeedback and she was not appealing from a compensation denial for an industrial insurance claim; Wash. Admin. Code § 296-21-280 did not apply. Appellant's argument that Wash. Rev. Code § 18.71.011 was unconstitutionally vague was without merit and she failed to show any real overbreadth of § 18.71.011 when applied to her unlicensed EDT practice. Her conduct was legitimately regulated as the unlawful practice of medicine. Her claim that the DOH lacked jurisdiction over her was rejected because she was not a tribal member and the State had authority over her while she was on tribal lands. Because Wash. Rev. Code §§ 18.71.011 and 18.120.010 were not ambiguous, the rule of lenity did not apply. Expert testimony was properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

 

1511 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Miesse


No. 34635-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1771



June 28, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for certiorari filed at, 07/28/2008


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Miesse, 139 Wn. App. 1034, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1835 (2007)


DISPOSITION:  [*1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of a trial court (Washington), which required him to submit a biological sample for deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) identification purposes under Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754 and denied his Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8 motion to modify his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty and was sentenced to 60 months' confinement with a 60-month firearm enhancement for first degree robbery and 68 months for first degree burglary and second degree assault. Defendant argued that compelled DNA sampling violated the Washington State and United States Constitutions and that the trial court imposed an improper exceptional sentence. The court affirmed. The court held that the trial court's order to collect a DNA sample under Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754 did not disturb defendant's private affairs or violate his Wash. Const. art. I, § 7 rights because, as a convicted felon, he had no valid privacy interest in the collection of his DNA information for identification. The court held that the biological sampling met the special needs exception to the warrant requirement of the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court held that because the State charged defendant with a class A felony, the statutory maximum for his crime was life in prison under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.20.021(1)(a) and, thus, his 120-month sentence did not exceed the statutory maximum and did not violate his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1512 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Radcliffe


No. 34447-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


139 Wn. App. 214; 159 P.3d 486; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1511



June 12, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at State v. Radcliffe, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 257 (Wash., Mar. 5, 2008)
Review granted by State v. Radcliffe, 163 Wn.2d 1021, 180 P.3d 1293, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 272 (2008)
Affirmed by State v. Radcliffe, 164 Wn.2d 900, 194 P.3d 250, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1038 (Wash., Oct. 23, 2008)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Washington trial court found defendant guilty of two counts of third degree child rape and one count of indecent liberties with forcible compulsion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting the statements he gave to the police. With respect to finding of fact number nine, defendant maintained that he unequivocally requested a lawyer during a police officer's questioning. Defendant testified that he said he wanted a lawyer multiple times but the officer merely continued his questioning. But, the officer testified that defendant said only that he did not know if he needed a lawyer and that defendant never specifically asked for an attorney. The officer's testimony provided substantial support for the trial court's finding that defendant stated that he did not know if he needed a lawyer. After a knowing and voluntary waiver of the Miranda rights, the officer could continue questioning unless and until defendant unequivocally requested an attorney. Because defendant's reference to an attorney was equivocal, the officer was not obligated to stop his questioning or to clarify defendant's statement. Accordingly, the trial court properly admitted defendant's statements at trial pursuant to the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Johnson


No. 57056-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1493



June 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Johnson, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1625 (Wash. Ct. App., June 11, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from a trial court (Washington), which convicted him of unlawful delivery and possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence, he was convicted of unlawful delivery and possession of cocaine. As part of his sentence, the trial court ordered him to provide a biological sample for Deoxyribonucleic Acid (DNA) identification analysis pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred when it ruled that the arresting officer did not need to disclose what a "good buy" sign was at the suppression hearing. The court found that even without any testimony about a "good buy" sign, the State had a strong case against defendant. Before encountering defendant, the cooperating witness (CW) had money, but no cocaine. The CW returned with cocaine, but no money. The CW testified that he purchased the cocaine from defendant. The arresting officer testified that he witnessed actions consistent with a drug transaction between the CW and defendant. Further, the compelled collection of DNA from a convicted felon did not invade a recognized private affair under the Washington Constitution or the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1514 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Snyder


No. 57639-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1479



June 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Snyder, 139 Wn. App. 1009, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1599 (Wash. Ct. App., June 11, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to distribution of a controlled substance to a minor, second degree burglary, and unlawful harboring of a minor. The trial court (Washington) denied defendant's request for the Drug Offender Sentencing Alternative (DOSA), Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.660, and sentenced defendant to concurrent sentences of 84 months, 22 months, and 6 months. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court abused its discretion and that compelled collection of DNA from convicted felons under Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754 was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found that the trial court relied on defendant's prior criminal history of failing to obey court orders and that the offense involved distributing drugs to a teenager. These facts were properly before the court and did not violate the "real facts" doctrine. The trial court determined that defendant was not a suitable candidate for the DOSA because he had a history of failing to comply with court orders and distributed drugs to a teenager, and the trial court believed that the program would not be effective to rehabilitate him. The trial court properly exercised its discretion. Before entering his guilty plea, the trial court informed defendant that there was no guarantee that he would receive a DOSA, and defendant responded that he understood. Defendant was properly informed that he might not receive a DOSA. The compelled collection of DNA from convicted felons under Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754 did not violate either the Washington Constitution or the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence.

 

1515 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Lehto v. Sequoia Voting Sys., Inc.


No. 58138-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1490



June 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Lehto v. Sequoia Voting Sys., Inc., 139 Wn. App. 1011, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1603 (Wash. Ct. App., June 11, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voters sought review of an order from a trial court (Washington), which granted a motion to dismiss filed by defendants, a county and a voting machine manufacturer, in an action for invalidation of the contract between defendants.


OVERVIEW: In the 2004 general election, the county polls used electronic voting machines. After the election, the governing regulations were amended to require that any electronic voting system produce individual paper records. The electronic voting machines could no longer be used. The voters brought an action against defendants, seeking invalidation of the contract between defendants on the ground that the confidentiality provisions violated voters' fundamental right to suffrage by preventing access to information by which voters could personally verify the accuracy of the election. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim. On appeal, the court found that the relief the voters sought, voiding the contract between defendants, would not directly redress their claimed injury. Voiding the contract would not automatically release the allegedly withheld information. It would not alter the results of the uncontested election in which the voters claimed that their votes were diluted. Because the election was over, the machines were no longer in use, and the challenged contract had been fully performed, the appeal, and the entire case, was moot.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal as moot.

 

1516 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Tukwila Sch. Dist. No. 406 v. City of Tukwila


No. 58178-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


140 Wn. App. 735; 167 P.3d 1167; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1491



June 11, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: Order Granting Motion to Publish September 10, 2007.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Tukwila Sch. Dist. No. 406 v. City of Tukwila, 139 Wn. App. 1011, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1594 (Wash. Ct. App., June 11, 2007)


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sued respondent city, seeking a declaratory judgment and tax refund challenging the city's storm and surface water utility charge under Wash. Const. art. VII, § 1. The trial court (Washington) denied the school district's motion to strike an expert's statements and dismissed the complaint on summary judgment. The school district appealed.


OVERVIEW: The school district challenged the city's storm and surface water utility charge under Wash. Rev. Code §§ 35.67.010, 35.67.020, and 35.67.120 on the ground that it was an unlawful tax imposed in violation of the uniformity requirement of Wash. Const. art. VII, § 1. The appellate court determined that the city was properly granted summary judgment because the charge was a permissible regulatory fee. The charge was not a tax under the Covell factors, because (1) its purpose was limited to protecting property owners and local water sources from harm caused by storm and surface water runoff, (2) the city segregated the funds and used them only for this purpose, and (3) the fee was roughly proportional to the amount of impervious surface on the property being taxed. Regarding the school district's argument that the trial court erred by admitting expert testimony on the issue of the reasonableness of the fee, any error was harmless because while the expert opinion was irrelevant to the issue before the trial court, the trial court expressly stated that it did not rely on this testimony to make its decision.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

 

1517 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baldwin


No. 23291-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1431



June 5, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 04-1-00706-3. Judge signing: KATHLEEN M. O'CONNOR. Date filed: August 12, 2004.
State v. Baldwin, 139 Wn. App. 1003, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1553 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Washington) convicted defendant of first degree theft and first degree robbery. Defendant was given an exceptional sentence of 120 months on his conviction for first degree robbery on the ground that the victim was particularly vulnerable due to her advanced age. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the State presented insufficient evidence of accomplice liability and challenged the trial court's exceptional sentence in the absence of specific jury findings. The appellate court concluded there was sufficient evidence that defendant had general knowledge of the robbery and aided in the planning and commission of the offense based on evidence that defendant and his accomplice were driving around with the specific and sole purpose of looking for opportunities to steal. Defendant was not required to have specific knowledge that the victim was injured or that his accomplice intended to actually injure her, as this element merely elevated the robbery charge to first degree. Further, defendant's waiver containing an express statement that he wished to have the judge decide beyond a reasonable doubt whether an aggravating circumstance existed supported the imposition of an exceptional sentence. Moreover, defendant knowingly waived his right to a jury fact finding of any aggravating circumstances. Thus, the trial court had the statutory authority to engage in fact finding in support of an exceptional sentence based on defendant's express waiver.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1518 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Clear Channel Outdoor, Inc. v. Schrem P'ship


No. 57326-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1401



June 4, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Clear Channel Outdoor, Inc. v. Schrem P'ship, 138 Wn. App. 1060, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1597 (Wash. Ct. App., June 4, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee lessor found during discovery that neither appellant lessee nor its predecessor obtained permits for billboards from the Washington State Department of Transportation (WSDOT) as required by the Scenic Vista Act (SVA). The trial court (Washington) granted the lessor's motion for partial summary judgment dismissing the lessee's claim for damages. The trial court held that the billboards were unlawful under the SVA. The lessee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The billboards were subject to the SVA. The sign was visible from the interstate system. Failure to obtain the permit removed the lessee from any protection afforded by the SVA. Moreover, the SVA itself provided that any sign erected or maintained contrary to the provisions of the chapter or rules that was designed to be viewed from the interstate system, the primary system, or the scenic system was a public nuisance. The billboards constituted a public nuisance. Thus, the lessee's lease was subject to the notice of unlawful detainer by the lessor. The lessee argued that no action could be brought against it because it was a legal nonconforming use and the SVA required compensation be paid before requiring removal of the signs. But, in order to come under the umbrella of just compensation under the SVA, the lessee would have had to have legally erected the signs and be "in compliance with existing state and local law." Since the billboards were unlawful when erected in 1987 and were deemed to be a public nuisance until their removal in 2005, the lessee had no right to compensation for the billboards. The trial court's award of attorney fees to the lessor was not in error.


OUTCOME: The trial court's summary judgment dismissal of all of the lessee's claims and the trial court's award of attorney fees were affirmed. Additionally, the lessor was entitled to attorney fees on appeal under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.84.330 and Wash. R. App. P. 18.1.
