State v. Meents


No. 34330-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 337



February 27, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Meents, 137 Wn. App. 1025, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1027 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court convicted defendant of bail jumping and two counts of third degree assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the information omitted an essential element of bail jumping, that the knowledge instruction given to the jury contained an unlawful mandatory presumption as well as confusing language, and that his assault convictions were based on a judicially created and thus unconstitutional definition of assault. The appellate court found that there was sufficient language in the bail jumping charge to inform defendant that he was being charged with having failed to make a court appearance of which he had knowledge. Regardless of the shortcomings in the charging document, defendant had notice of the proper knowledge requirement. The trial court's knowledge instruction did not violate defendant's right to due process. Defendant's challenge to his assault convictions were rejected.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1562 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hutchins


No. 24559-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 346



February 27, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Hutchins, 137 Wn. App. 1026, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1039 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court, Benton County. Docket No. 03-1-00186-8. CAMERON MITCHELL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Superior Court, Benton County, Washington, defendant was convicted of first degree child molestation and communication with a minor for immoral purposes. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant called a four-year-old child's parents and asked if she could come over to play with his son. When the child returned home, she told her mother and a counselor that defendant had touched her vagina and watched a pornographic movie. The appellate court determined that the admission of the child's statements under the child hearsay statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.120, did not violate defendant's confrontation rights under the Sixth Amendment and Wash. Const. art. I, § 22 because the statements were not testimonial since the statements were not solicited and the purpose of the mother and the counselor in talking to the child was not investigative. The statements were properly admitted under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.120 and the Ryan factors because, inter alia, the child had no motive to lie, the statements were consistent, and the statements were made without prompting. In addition, it was not an abuse of discretion to exclude evidence that the child's father was a sexual offender, because defendant failed to establish the required nexus since the father's criminal history alone was insufficient to establish an act or step taken towards committing these crimes.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

Schlegel v. Dep't of Licensing


No. 24314-1-III consolidated with No. 24400-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


137 Wn. App. 364; 153 P.3d 244; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 347



February 27, 2007, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence (DUI) in the district court. The Department of Licensing (DOL) suspended defendant's license. The Superior Court, Kittitas County, Washington, dismissed the DUI charge and reversed DOL's suspension order based on an impermissible stop under Wash. Rev. Code § 77.15.080. The State sought review.


OVERVIEW: A Washington Department of Fish and Wildlife officer stopped defendant's vehicle because he observed (1) the vehicle on the opening day of elk hunting season inside an elk hunting area, (2) that the occupants wore hunting clothing, and (3) that the vehicle was consistent with the type that hunters used on a poorly maintained dirt hunting road. The officer saw that the occupants possessed elk rifles in the truck-cab, and a passenger stated that they had been elk hunting. The officer smelled alcohol on defendant's breath. Defendant contended that the stop was unconstitutional because it constituted an illegal roadblock. Under Wash. R. App. Dec. Ct. Ltd. J. 9.1 and Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.308, the appellate court determined that the brief investigatory stop was lawful under Wash. Rev. Code § 77.15.080(1) because articulable facts existed indicating defendant was engaged in hunting activities when first observed by the officer. Also, the record showed that the officer did not stop every passing vehicle, but restricted his brief investigatory stops to situations where he had articulable facts that the passersby were engaged in hunting activities.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the superior court and affirmed defendant's district court conviction for DUI and his DOL license suspension.

 

1564 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Bahl


No. 56812-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


137 Wn. App. 709; 159 P.3d 416; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 324



February 26, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Order Granting Motion to Publish March 19, 2007.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Bahl, 137 Wn. App. 1021, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1010 (2007)
Review granted by State v. Bahl, 162 Wn.2d 1011, 175 P.3d 1094, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 2 (2008)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Bahl, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1032 (Wash., Oct. 9, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After convicting defendant of second degree rape and first degree burglary, the trial court (Washington) imposed an indeterminate sentence of 105 months to life for the rape and a concurrent sentence of 34 months for the burglary. Defendant was also sentenced to a lifetime of community custody under the supervision of the department of corrections. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant challenged several conditions of his community custody, contending that the prohibitions concerning "erotic material and sexual stimulus materia" were overbroad and vague, in violation of his right to free speech. The appellate court found that defendant's argument failed to recognize that he was not complaining about a statute affecting the public generally, but was attempting to invoke the overbreadth doctrine to attack a condition of his own particular sentence. Defendant was shown to be egregiously unable to control himself when in a state of sexual stimulus, and an order limiting his access to sexually stimulating materials and environments related directly to that aspect of his crime. Because the conditions were crime-related, defendant's overbreadth argument was unfounded. And because defendant did not explain why his vagueness challenge required evaluation of the conditions in a factual vacuum, the appellate court declined to review it. Denial of defendant's mistrial motion did not affect the outcome as the jury demonstrated that it could put aside any improper prejudice from a prosecutor's comment by refusing to convict defendant on other charges.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1565 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Home Builders v. City of Bainbridge Island


NO. 34743-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


137 Wn. App. 338; 153 P.3d 231; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 318



February 21, 2007, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, home builders, filed a class action lawsuit against respondent, City of Bainbridge Island, concerning payment of building permit fees. The Washington trial court found that the City's fees for building permits were reasonable and did not violate Wash. Rev. Code § 82.02.020. The builders appealed.


OVERVIEW: The City Council adopted a resolution increasing the building permit fees. The builders challenged whether the City's fees fell within the allowed statutory exceptions to Wash. Rev. Code § 82.02.020. The appellate court found that the burden of showing that the fees complied with a statutory exception and were reasonable rested with the City because the fees were, by statute, an exception to the general prohibition against fees on construction and development. The appellate court found that the case would need to be remanded for further proceedings allocating the burden of proof to the City. The only issue at trial was whether the City's costs and the resulting fees, were reasonable, which prevented the builders' challenge to whether the imposed fees were an allowable exception because the City was not required to show that the fee calculation was limited to the legislatively specified costs of processing applications, inspecting and reviewing plans, or preparing State Environmental Policy Act statements. Also, the trial court should have focused on evidence of costs specifically allowed in the statute to calculate the permit fees.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court to determine whether the City's fees were limited to those the Washington Legislature specified, and if so, reasonable in light of the statutory limitations placed on the fees the City could impose.

 

1566 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hamilton


No. 56947-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 293



February 20, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Hamilton, 137 Wn. App. 1017, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 998 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the King County Superior Court (Washington), defendant was convicted of felony harassment and first-degree burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State conceded that defendant's felony harassment conviction had to be reversed because the trial court failed to provide the jury with an instruction defining the term threat, an instruction that should have incorporated the standard for what constituted a "true threat." However, the court rejected defendant's prosecutorial misconduct argument because it was not misconduct for the prosecutor to argue from facts in evidence or suggest reasonable inferences from the evidence. The prosecuting attorney's argument that defendant's version of the events was improbable was directed toward the content of defendant's contradicted testimony and did not impinge upon defendant's exercise of his right to testify and present evidence. Further, defense counsel's decision not to move for a mistrial was neither deficient performance nor prejudicial. Several of the objections defendant's trial counsel raised during the prosecuting attorney's closing argument were sustained by the trial court, and the remainder of the prosecuting attorney's argument was not improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree burglary and reversed his conviction for felony harassment. The court remanded the cause for resentencing on the burglary conviction and a new trial on the harassment allegation.

State v. Poma


23862-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 231



February 13, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Poma, 137 Wn. App. 1014, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 989 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 03-1-00954-1. Judge signing: DENNIS D. YULE (TRIAL), VIC L. VANDERSCHOOR (SUPPRESSION). Date filed: February 18, 2005, October 18, 2004 (SUPPRESSION).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of a trial court in Benton County, Washington, which convicted him of unlawful possession of a controlled substance and theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was a passenger in a vehicle that was pulled over for driving without lighted headlights, argued that he received ineffective assistance of counsel because defense counsel's motion to suppress failed to raise the issue of whether lighted headlights were required. Defendant maintained that lighted headlights were not required under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.37.020 at the time of the stop. The court concluded that defendant failed to establish his representation was deficient. There was no testimony indicating that lighted headlights were not needed. Section 46.37.020 did not limit its coverage to the time period from a half hour after sunset to a half hour before sunrise. Although defendant urged the court to take judicial notice of the time of sunset on the date of arrest, Wash. R. App. P. 9.11 restricted the court's consideration of adjudicative facts not already found in the record. Defendant failed to meet the test set forth in the rule. Even if the court had taken judicial notice as requested by defendant, the time of sunset would not have been dispositive. The court also concluded that defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Custody of A.C.


No. 22930-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


137 Wn. App. 245; 153 P.3d 203; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 237



February 13, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by In re Custody of Angelo, 175 P.3d 1093, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 877 (Wash., 2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by In re Custody of v. Cork, 2009 Wash. LEXIS 74 (Wash., Feb. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
In re A.F.-C., 2001 MT 283, 307 Mont. 358, 37 P.3d 724, 2001 Mont. LEXIS 547 (2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant birth mother sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which granted nonparental custody to respondent foster parents under Washington's Uniform Child Custody Jurisdiction and Enforcement Act (UCCJEA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 26.27. The trial court found that the mother was not unfit but that continued placement of the child with her would detrimentally affect the child's development.


OVERVIEW: The State of Montana had first placed the child with the foster parents, but temporary investigative authority was eventually terminated when the mother fulfilled requirements of a treatment plan. The mother and child moved to Washington, after which the present action was filed by the foster parents. On review, the court found no error. Under Wash. Rev. Code §§ 26.27.201(1) and 26.27.021(7), although neither Washington nor Montana were the child's home state, there were significant connections with Washington. Thus, the trial court properly assumed subject matter jurisdiction under the UCCJEA. Further, the decision to retain jurisdiction was not unreasonable under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.27.261 in light of the fact that the mother lived in the state and the request for the trial court to decline jurisdiction was made a week before trial. Finally, despite the fact that the trial court stated language concerning the best interest of the child, the trial court's findings and its oral ruling clearly established that it applied the heightened actual-detriment-to-the-child standard required for determining custody between a parent and a nonparent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1569 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Strickland


No. 34043-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 204



February 7, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Strickland, 137 Wn. App. 1005, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 738 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of attempted first degree theft for trying to steal a vehicle. He appealed and argued that the attempt statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.28.020, violated the separation of powers doctrine; the jury instructions were inadequate; he received ineffective assistance of counsel; and his sentence was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.28.020, which defined criminal attempt, was unconstitutional because it failed to define all essential elements of the offense and therefore required the judiciary to encroach on core legislative functions. However, this claim failed because the court had already rejected this argument in a different case, and defendant provided no reason to deviate from that precedent. As to defendant's jury instruction challenges, defendant was correct that one instruction misstated the law of attempt. However, when reading the challenged jury instruction with the other instructions, the error was rendered harmless because another instruction included the missing intent element. Because the jury instructions did not mislead the jury, defendant's attorney's decision not to object to them was reasonable and did not prejudice defendant. Finally, the evidence was insufficient to prove defendant's criminal history. Defendant's generic agreement that he had been convicted of 10 unspecified prior felony convictions during his sentencing allocution was not a waiver and was insufficient to support the trial court's findings of fact.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but remanded for resentencing.

 

1570 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Young v. Kitsap County


NO. 34050-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 191



February 6, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Young v. Kitsap County, 137 Wn. App. 1003, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 729 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent county initiated a public nuisance abatement action against appellant property owner under Kitsap County, Wash., Code § 9.56, the Public Nuisances ordinance, for having inoperable vehicles on his property. The Mason County Superior Court (Washington) affirmed the county's abatement action and denied the property owner's constitutional challenges to the ordinance. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner's vagueness challenge to the ordinance failed because the terms the property owner pointed to were not inherently subjective. Also, Kitsap County, Wash., Code § 9.56.060(2) provided that anyone who had been subject to the summary abatement process had a right to receive a notice as soon as reasonably possible after the abatement (i.e. before the action was finalized). Thus, the summary abatement process did not violate procedural due process requirements. The ordinance did not violate substantive due process rights because Kitsap County, Wash., Code § 9.56.035 required the county to use less restrictive means before proceeding with abatement unless the conditions warranting abatement imposed an immediate threat to the public, and the ordinance prohibited only vehicle lots that did not have county approval. Also, Wash. Rev. Code § 46.04.125 did not deal with public nuisances and, therefore, was not in conflict with the ordinance. Finally, the ordinance did not violate the single subject requirement of Wash. Const. art. II, § 19 because all of its provisions facilitated the deterrence of abatable nuisances.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court was affirmed.

 

1571 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Glave


No. 33171-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 146



January 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay granted by Glave v. Glebe, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 119811 (W.D. Wash., Oct. 17, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Glave, 136 Wn. App. 1055, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 616 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a Washington trial court of first degree child rape and first degree attempted child rape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his Confrontation Clause rights were violated when a nurse testified to hearsay statements the complainant made because the statements were testimonial and the complainant was unavailable for cross-examination regarding her statement to the nurse. The court of appeals disagreed. The complainant took the stand and defendant cross-examined her regarding the statements she allegedly made to the nurse. The complainant could not recall what she said to the nurse, but she did independently identify defendant as her rapist. Defendant also cross-examined the complainant about the identification. In addition, the trial court's ruling that defendant could ask an officer why he was on paid administrative leave but could not ask him whether he did in fact falsify a police report was proper. Defendant asked the officer whether he was on administrative leave, what he was charged with, and which government entity charged him. Because the only additional evidence that defendant could have elicited would have been the officer's invocation of his Fifth Amendment rights, the danger of unfair prejudice outweighed the evidence's probative value.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

1573 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ryan


No. 55871-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 130



January 29, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Ryan, 136 Wn. App. 1051, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 600 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both defendant and the State appealed a judgment of a trial court (Washington), which, upon resentencing, imposed a firearm enhancement and determined that defendant's three kidnapping convictions merged with his robbery conviction. The trial court imposed a single, standard range sentence of 68 months plus one firearm enhancement for the robbery conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant restrained four people at gunpoint while robbing an auto parts store. The court remanded the action after reversing defendant's life sentence. On appeal after the resentencing, the court held that first degree kidnapping, even when incidental to a first degree robbery, did not merge with a robbery conviction because proof of kidnapping was not necessary to prove first degree robbery, and proof of first degree kidnapping required only the intent to commit robbery, not the completion of robbery. The trial court's other findings that defendant produced a fully-functional, loaded nine millimeter firearm and pointed it at the four people inside the store and that defendant continued to hold one victim at gunpoint showed overwhelmingly that defendant committed the robbery using a firearm. The enhanced sentence for defendant's use of a firearm did not violate double jeopardy principles or Blakely. While a finding of ineffectiveness of counsel could in certain circumstances imply a conflict of interest, defendant affirmatively acknowledged on the record that he was satisfied with his representation and had no reservations in having the same attorney represent him at the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the imposition of the firearm enhancement but reversed the convictions and remanded for resentencing on the issue of the merger of kidnapping and robbery.

State v. Simpson


No. 24725-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


136 Wn. App. 812; 150 P.3d 1167; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 116



January 25, 2007, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court in Spokane County (Washington), which imposed restrictions on defendant's sentence under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.505(8).


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to a sex offense involving a minor. As a condition of his community custody release, the trial court required defendant to obtain the explicit consent of every sex partner, as well as the approval of his therapist and community corrections officer, prior to his engaging in future sexual activity. Defendant appealed, contending that these restrictions were not reasonably related to the crime under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.030(12) (2003) (now codified at § 9.94A.030(13), In affirming, the appellate court held that the condition of consent from a prospective sexual partner was reasonable, even though the condition applied to adults, because defendant had a problem recognizing consent. Next, the consent restriction did not violate the right to due process, and it was not unconstitutionally vague. A person of ordinary understanding could have recognized a violation. The fact that the precise meaning of consent was situational did not mean the prohibition was vague. Finally, the requirement for official approval was reasonably related to the offense. If it became too intrusive, defendant was permitted to seek relief via a personal restraint petition.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1575 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



New W. Fisheries, Inc. v. Hough


No. 55535-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 46



January 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at New W. Fisheries v. Hough, 136 Wn. App. 1038, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 505 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client challenged a judgment of the Whatcom County trial court (Washington) dismissing on summary judgment under Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 56(c) its legal malpractice action against appellee attorneys and dismissal of its second amended complaint against one of the attorneys. One attorney cross-appealed, challenging the trial court's decision to grant the client's motion to file a second amended complaint against him.


OVERVIEW: The client hired the first attorney to sue the city for damages allegedly caused by the city's misrepresentations and breach of a property exchange agreement. The first attorney failed to file a pre-suit claim for damages with the city as required by Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96, and the client's lawsuits against the city were dismissed. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly dismissed the client's legal malpractice action against the first attorney because it was barred by three-year statute of limitations of Wash. Rev. Code § 4.16.080(3). The client knew in 1997, when it received a letter from the second attorney, that a pre-suit tort claim for damages was mandatory, that there was no evidence that a claim was filed, and that the city could successfully seek dismissal for failure to file the claim, but the client did not file its legal malpractice action until 2002. However, the trial court erred by dismissing the client's action against the second attorney because there were material issues of fact about when the client knew or should have known about the discrepancy between the property exchange and the city ordinance imposing an easement.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the client's malpractice action against the first attorney was affirmed. However, the judgment dismissing the client's malpractice claim against the second attorney was reversed. The judgment granting the client's motion to file a second amended complaint against the second attorney was affirmed.

In re Dependency of T.L.G.


No. 57862-6-I (consolidated with 57863-4-I, 57864-2-I, 57865-1-I, 58560-6-I &, 58561-4-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


139 Wn. App. 1; 156 P.3d 222; 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 62



January 16, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals April 23, 2007.] Order Granting Motion to Publish April 19, 2007.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended by, On reconsideration by In re Dependency of T.L.G., 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 800 (Wash. Ct. App., Apr. 23, 2007)
Related proceeding at In re Dependency of T.L.G., 2011 Wash. App. LEXIS 1613 (Wash. Ct. App., July 18, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: T.L.G. v. Dep't of Soc. & Health Servs., 136 Wn. App. 1041, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 517 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged a judgment of a Washington juvenile court suspending visitation with the parents' dependent children. The father appealed an order prohibiting him from disseminating any documents, reports, and orders without permission of the juvenile court and notice to the Department of Social and Health Services (DSHS) and his children's volunteer guardian ad litem.


OVERVIEW: Visitation between the parents and their children was suspended in 2002 after an altercation between the father and a security guard during a scheduled visit in the presence of one of the children. On appeal, the court held that the juvenile court misapplied Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.136(1)(b)(ii) (2004) by denying the parents visitation as a sanction and without a showing of actual harm. The DSHS had made no attempts to reunite the family. A doctor's anger management evaluations that the State relied on to support the suspension of visitation did not address how the parents' anger management issues or clinical profiles would pose a risk to their children in the context of a supervised visit. One incident, nearly five years ago, was an insufficient basis to deny all visitation between the parents and their young children. The court also reversed the juvenile court's order prohibiting the father from disseminating any information without permission and notice because the record did not contain a sufficient basis to support such a broad restriction on the father's speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment suspending the parents' visitation was reversed, and the case was remanded to the juvenile court with directions to require the DSHS to take immediate steps toward reunifying the family. The order prohibiting the father from disseminating information about the case was reversed and the case was remanded to the juvenile court with directions to schedule an immediate hearing to determine whether a protective order was necessary.

State v. Autrey


No. 24670-1-III linked w/ No. 24952-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


136 Wn. App. 460; 150 P.3d 580; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2835



December 28, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, convicted defendants of rape and sexual assault of minors, and ordered one defendant to 111 months confinement, including community custody conditions, and the other defendant had community custody conditions. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the trial court erred by imposing community custody conditions requiring them to obtain explicit consent before sexual contact and prior approval from their therapist and Community Corrections Officer. The appellate court found that the "explicit consent" requirement was reasonably crime-related. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by finding this condition reasonably necessary to accomplish the State's purpose of protecting the public. The issue of the victim's consent would be decided beyond a reasonable doubt. The offender's freedom of choosing even adult sexual partners was reasonably related to their crimes because potential romantic partners may be responsible for the safety of live-in or visiting minors. The trial court did not err in reasoning that one defendant's victim's mother was unable to protect her daughter and denying defendant's Special Sexual Offender Sentencing Alternative (SSOSA) request where defendant was marginally qualified for a SSOSA and the mother failed to protect her daughter for two years. Defendant's issue concerning a community custody condition was not ripe for review as a search had not taken place.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

Neighbors for Responsible Dev. v. City of Yakima


No. 24857-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2810



December 21, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Neighbors v. City of Yakima, 136 Wn. App. 1026, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 3051 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: YAKIMA. Docket No(s): 02-2-02689-2. Judge signing: MICHAEL E. COOPER. Date filed: December 23, 2005.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee developer and city entered into a development agreement regarding a certain piece of property. Appellant nonprofit organization filed a land use appeal, seeking a declaratory judgment that the agreement was unenforceable. The Superior Court, Yakima County (Washington), dismissed the action, finding the organization's appeal was time-barred by Wash. Rev. Code ch. 36.70C. The organization appealed.


OVERVIEW: On November 20, 2001, the city council authorized and approved the agreement. Under Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C.040(4)(b), that was the date the appeal period began. The organization did not file its petition for review of the land use decision and complaint for declaratory judgment until September 6, 2002. The petition was untimely. At the latest, the organization had actual notice of the agreement on April 15, 2002. It nonetheless failed to file an appeal within 21 days of that date. Also, the organization's due process argument against the rezoning failed because notice informed the public that the purpose of a public meeting was to consider the recommendation on the rezone, there were comments on the city council's proposed changes, and the council's changes did not materially alter the impact of the rezone as recommended by the hearing examiner. There was no evidence the agreement predetermined the outcome of the rezone or that the rezone was arbitrary and unreasonable. The evidence established the rezone was for the general welfare of the community and that evidence was independent of the agreement.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1579 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Pers. Restraint of Reed


No. 24352-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SIX


136 Wn. App. 352; 149 P.3d 415; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2796



December 19, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT, STEVENS COUNTY. Superior Court No: 18649. Superior Court Judge signing: SIDNEY BUCKLEY. Date filed in Superior Court: 10/26/73.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought relief from personal restraint imposed for a conviction imposed by the Superior Court, Stevens County (Washington) upon plea of guilty to two counts of second degree murder under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.48.040(2). Petitioner received concurrent sentences of up to life in prison. Petitioner claimed that the judgment and sentence were facially invalid and that his convictions had to be vacated.


OVERVIEW: The dispositive question was whether the rationale of a prior case adopting the merger rule that assault could not be the predicate crime for felony murder applied to second degree felony murder crimes predicated on assault under former § 9.48.040(2) (1909). The court dismissed petitioner's application for relief as untimely under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090(1) in that no exception to the one-year time bar applied. The court concluded that based upon the language of the amended information, the guilty plea statement, the judgment, and the sentence documents, petitioner was charged and convicted solely of second degree felony murder predicated upon assault. However, his judgment and sentence evinced no facial invalidity, and petitioner thus showed no constitutional error. The prior case adopted the merger rule for a conviction under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.32.050; however, the state supreme court had repeatedly rejected the merger rule as applied to former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.48.040(2), the statute under which petitioner was convicted. There was a clear legislative intent that second degree felony murder under § 9.48.040(2) could be predicated upon assault.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition.

 

1580 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Saben v. Skagit County


No. 57390-0-I,


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


136 Wn. App. 869; 152 P.3d 1034; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2740



December 18, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Order Granting Respondents' Motion to Publish filed February 7, 2007.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Saben v. Skagit County, 136 Wn. App. 1023, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 3011 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order from a trial court (Washington), which awarded summary judgment and damages to respondent property owners in an action for the issuance of building permits on theories of contract and estoppel.


OVERVIEW: The owners agreed to purchase property, contingent on the availability of building permits. The county issued three of four permits. The owners closed on the property. The county later denied a permit for their residence and revoked the permits for the garage, shop, and septic system. The county subsequently agreed to reinstate the revoked permits and grant a single-family residence permit. The county later denied the single-family residence permit. The county left the permits for the garage, shop, and septic system intact. The owners brought an action, seeking issuance of the permits on theories of contract and estoppel. The trial court awarded summary judgment to the owners, ordering the county to issue the permits. On appeal, the court found that the only reasonable inference from the evidence was that a deal was made and the owners, at least, performed. Whatever public policy the county's interpretive uncertainties might express, it could not trump the county's obligation to honor its settlement with the owners. The trial court properly determined that the county acted arbitrarily and capriciously and that the owners were entitled to damages under Wash. Rev. Code § 64.40.020.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order requiring the county to issue the permits and finding the county liable for damages. The court remanded the case for the determination of damages.

 

1581 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Herbert v. Pub. Disclosure Comm'n


Nos. 57502-3-I, 57503-1-I (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


136 Wn. App. 249; 148 P.3d 1102; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2746



December 18, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, public school teachers, appealed from the Superior Court, King County, Washington, which affirmed appellee state public disclosure commission's ruling against the teachers who claimed that the constitutionality of Wash. Rev. Code ch. 42.17.13, as applied to them, did not pass strict scrutiny as a restriction on their First Amendment free speech rights and that the statute as applied was arbitrary and capricious and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The teachers were fined by the commission for using school facilities in violation of Wash. Rev. Code ch. 42.17.130's prohibition on the use of public resources for political advocacy. The court began its First Amendment analysis by noting that school internal mail or computer systems were not traditionally forums for public communication, and there was no evidence that the high school opened either its mailbox or computer system to the public. Thus, the school's internal mail and computer systems were nonpublic forums. Because these forums are nonpublic, the court had to determine whether the regulation on their use was reasonable in light of their purpose and viewpoint neutral. The court concluded that the commission's interpretation of ch. 42.17.130 - restricting the use of the internal school mailboxes and the e-mail system - was reasonable and viewpoint-neutral. Furthermore, pure political speech was permitted, but using the facilities to deliver speech was prohibited. This distinction was rational and reasonable in light of ch. 42.17.130's policy goals of ensuring that public facilities were used for their intended purposes and in maintaining the state's political neutrality.


OUTCOME: The trial court's holding in favor of the commission was affirmed.

 

1582 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Watkins


No. 56507-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


136 Wn. App. 240; 148 P.3d 1112; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2748



December 18, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at State v. Watkins, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 779 (Wash., Oct. 2, 2007)
Review denied by State v. Watkins, 161 Wn.2d 1028, 172 P.3d 360, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 803 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Watkins v. Washington, 552 U.S. 1282, 128 S. Ct. 1707, 170 L. Ed. 2d 518, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2749 (2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Watkins v. Uttecht, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 79944 (W.D. Wash., Aug. 6, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with four counts of rape of a child in the first degree. Defendant moved to suppress his confession. The Superior Court, King County, Washington found that defendant's statements were admissible. The jury convicted defendant as charged. Defendant appealed, alleging that the trial court denied him his constitutional right to a unanimous jury verdict by failing to give a proper unanimity instruction.


OVERVIEW: At trial, two minors testified that defendant repeatedly had oral sex with them and would touch their breasts and bottoms on multiple occasions. The court admitted into evidence defendant's taped confession and allowed the State to play it for the jury. Defendant denied the allegations and argued that his confession was coerced and false. The State proposed and the court gave the unanimity instruction that was at issue in the instant case. Defendant claimed that the unanimity instruction given failed to make manifestly clear that the jury had to be unanimous as to the act that served as a basis for conviction. Jury instructions had to more than adequately convey the law. They had to make the relevant legal standard manifestly apparent to the average juror. In the present case, the unanimity instruction given to the jury arguably did not meet this standard. But the instant court was bound by precedent from the state supreme court that expressly approved the unanimity instruction given. Accordingly, defendant's argument that the instruction failed to protect his constitutional right to a unanimous jury failed.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the trial court's judgment and sentence of defendant.

 

1583 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. NB


No. 33045-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2710



December 12, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. N.B., 136 Wn. App. 1016, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2984 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defendant appealed his juvenile adjudications for unlawful possession of a controlled substance, possession and use of drug paraphernalia, and second degree identity theft, on the grounds hat the trial court erred when it denied his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: The police received a call from an anonymous informant, who reported that a vehicle prowl was in progress. The informant identified the vehicle's make and color. When the officers arrived, defendant and another individual were walking near the vehicle described by the informant. The officers stopped defendant and his friend and did a pat down search of defendant. The search revealed a pipe used to smoke methamphetamine and a credit card in the name of another person. The appellate court found that the record was devoid of any evidence to establish the reliability of the informant and the informant did not include any noninnocuous details of the alleged vehicle prowl. Therefore, the informant was not reliable and the information the informant provided could not provide the basis for a suspicion of criminal activity. Furthermore, defendant fully cooperated with the officers and was not threatening or dangerous. Since the pat down search that recovered the methamphetamine pipe was illegal, the evidence obtained during the pat down had to be suppressed. Therefore, there was no evidence to support defendant's arrest and the arrest was also unjustified.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the denial of the suppression motion and suppressed all evidence obtained during the search, both the methamphetamine pipe and the evidence of identify theft. Because the State's case against defendant rested exclusively on improperly seized evidence, the appellate court reversed and order the trial court to vacate defendant's adjudications.

State v. Conlee


No. 33397-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2712



December 12, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Conlee, 136 Wn. App. 1017, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2987 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was charged with second degree assault of a child under alternative prongs set forth in Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.130(1) and convicted. The trial court (Washington) imposed an exceptional sentence upward, sentencing appellant to 60 months: 48 months based on the presumptive range and six months for each of the two aggravating circumstances the jury found. Appellant filed an appeal, challenging his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: The eight-year-old daughter of appellant's girlfriend testified that appellant whipped her with a belt, picked her up by her neck, and flicked cigarette ashes on her. The jury found appellant guilty of second degree assault of a child and concluded that facts supported two aggravating circumstances, abuse of trust and particular vulnerability. The appellate court determined that sufficient evidence, based on the victim's testimony and medical testimony, showed that appellant assaulted the victim in the past in a manner that either resulted in bodily harm greater than transient pain or minor temporary marks or caused her physical pain equivalent to torture under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.130(1)(b). The trial court did not err in applying Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9.94A.535 and 9.94A.537 at sentencing, because the saving clause statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 10.01.040, did not apply since, inter alia, (1) Blakely did not declare Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535 facially unconstitutional, and (2) § 9.94A.535 only altered the procedure, not appellant's substantive rights, as appellant was eligible for the exceptional sentence before and after the amendment of § 9.94A.535.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

Cmty. Telecable v. City of Seattle, Dep't of Executive Admin.


No. 57491-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


136 Wn. App. 169; 149 P.3d 380; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2690



December 11, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Cmty. Telecable of Seattle, Inc. v. City of Seattle, Dep't of Executive Admin., 161 Wn.2d 1025, 169 P.3d 830, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 799 (2007)
Reversed by Cmty. Telecable of Seattle, Inc. v. Dep't of Executive Admin., 164 Wn.2d 35, 186 P.3d 1032, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 607 (Wash., June 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 03-2-36639-1 SEA. Date filed in Superior Court: December 14, 2005. Superior Court Judge Signing: Richard Jones.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent cable company sued appellant city for a refund of a tax paid pursuant to the city's telephone utility tax. The Superior Court, King County, Washington granted summary judgment in favor of the company. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company owned a cable transmission network. In additions to providing cable television, the company also provided high-speed Internet connection. The city imposed a telephone utility tax on entities that engaged in the business of transmitting data over a network in the city. The company asserted that the tax was illegal under Washington's Internet Tax Moratorium and the federal Internet Tax Freedom Act (ITFA). The appellate court found that the tax was not barred by Washington's Internet Tax Moratorium because the moratorium did not preclude the city from taxing revenue from data transmission activity via a cable transmission system. Network telephone services, which were taxed by the city as "telephone business", were not subject to Washington's Internet Tax Moratorium. The city's tax was exempt under the ITFA's grandfather clause because the tax was authorized by statute before October 1, 1998, the company had notice that the city taxed its data transmission activities before October 1, 1998, and the city generally collected the tax prior to October 1, 1998. The tax was not discriminatory because it applied uniformly to companies engaged in the telephone business.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the appellate court directed that judgment be entered in favor of the city.

 

1586 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Higgins


NO. 33833-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


136 Wn. App. 87; 147 P.3d 649; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2681



December 5, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from a trial court in Washington, which convicted him of domestic violence second degree assault under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.021(1)(c). Specifically, he challenged the denial of his motion to suppress evidence found during the execution of a search warrant.


OVERVIEW: A married couple were fighting after a day of drinking. The wife called police to let her in the house after defendant locked her out. After letting her in a door with a landlord's key, the officer heard a gunshot. The wife first stated that she had fired the gun, but then contended that defendant had done so. Police then obtained a search warrant authorizing the seizure of "certain evidence of a crime, to-wit: "assault 2nd DV." An affidavit described the incident and established probable cause to search for a gun, bullets, and other evidence relating to the shooting. Defendant's motion to suppress this evidence was denied, and he sought review. In reversing, the appellate court determined that the warrant violated the particularity clause of the Fourth Amendment. The items could have been stated with more particularity since this was done in the affidavit, and the affidavit was irrelevant since it was not incorporated by reference. Moreover, the general reference to evidence of domestic violence was insufficient because it authorized the seizure of items for which there was no probable cause. Finally, the warrant did not authorize the search just for illicit items.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for suppression of the evidence seized under the warrant.

State v. Allenbach


No. 33955-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


136 Wn. App. 95; 147 P.3d 644; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2685



December 5, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of forgery under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.60.020(1)(a)(b) and second degree identity theft under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.35.020(3). The trial court (Washington) denied appellant's motion to suppress and motion for a new trial and arrest of judgment. Appellant brought an appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant presented a check at a bank that was payable to appellant and was drawn on the account of a person who did not know or authorize appellant to use the checks. When a teller became suspicious, appellant left the bank without the check and identifying items. Appellant argued that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.35.005(1)'s definition of "financial information" was unconstitutionally vague as applied under U.S. Const. amend. V because it did not apprise citizens with fair warning of what conduct was prohibited. The appellate court rejected appellant's argument, finding that (1) § 9.35.005(1) provided a clear list of specific types of information that qualified as "financial information" for purposes of committing the crime of identity theft under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.35.020, and (2) the Wash. Rev. Code § 9.35.005(1)(a) phrase "account numbers and balances" was sufficient to apprise citizens that a blank check qualified as "financial information" for purposes of identity theft.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

 

1588 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Acrey


No. 56759-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


135 Wn. App. 938; 146 P.3d 1215; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2465



November 13, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who drained the retirement savings of an elderly man and accumulated more than $ 83,000 of debt in his name after she married him, pleaded guilty in the King County Superior Court, Washington, to theft, identity theft, and perjury. Pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.505(8), the trial judge prohibited defendant, as part of her sentence, from working as a caretaker for elderly or disabled individuals. Defendant appealed her sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial judge had no authority to prohibit her from working as a caretaker for elderly or disabled individuals. The court concluded that § 9.94A.505(8) authorized the trial judge to impose crime-related prohibitions as part of any sentence. Gaining the trust of a dependent person by offering services was an intrinsic part of defendant's criminal method. The trial judge acted within her discretion in prohibiting defendant from using that method to find new victims. Working as a caretaker for dependent persons would have provided many opportunities for similar violations of trust. Therefore, the prohibition was directly related to defendant's crime. Although it was unnecessary to support the prohibition, the record indicated that the victim was disabled, at least to some extent. The victim admitted signing documents without knowing what they were for. The record amply supported the prohibition imposed by the trial judge. The prohibition was not vague. The trial judge did not prohibit defendant from caring for children. Defendant was well able to predict the prohibition's application with adequate certainty.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

S. Kitsap Family Worship Ctr. v. Weir


No. 33399-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


135 Wn. App. 900; 146 P.3d 935; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2416



November 7, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, worship center and developers, challenged a judgment of the trial court (Washington) that dismissed their breach of contract claim against defendants congregation member and his wife; and that awarded defendants damages caused by the lis pendens under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.28.328(3) and attorney fees under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.84.330 and a real estate purchase and sale agreement (REPSA) attorney fee provision.


OVERVIEW: A congregation member provided a loan to the worship center in a sales agreement (SA), by which the center would transfer title to property to the member but retain an option to repurchase it. The developers claimed that they were the assignees of the repurchase option. A RESPA was later executed that did not mention the repurchase option. A suit was filed after the repurchase deadline passed and the member refused to sell the property to the center for the SA price. The trial court dismissed plaintiffs' claims, holding that the SA was unenforceable under the Statute of Frauds and that it had merged into the deed. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that the evidence supported the trial court's finding that the REPSA was fully integrated without reference to the repurchase option and that the center knowingly conveyed all title and interest by the deed. The court found that the member was entitled to damages and attorney fees under the lis pendens statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 4.28.328(3), because the center had no substantial justification for filing the lis pendens. However, the court reversed the fee award under the REPSA provision because that provision had merged into the deed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the trial court judgment that awarded defendants attorney fees under the RESPA provision, but affirmed the portion of the judgment dismissing plaintiffs' contract claims and awarding defendants damages and attorney fees for the improper lis pendens. The court remanded the case to the trial court to calculate fees and costs under the lis pendens statute. The court granted defendants attorney fees on appeal.

State v. Wrzesien


No. 33530-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2433



November 7, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Wrzesien, 135 Wn. App. 1040, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2880 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a Washington trial court of unlawful manufacture of methamphetamine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain her conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant testified that she did not know that any items associated with manufacturing methamphetamine were in the car, but police found numerous items used in manufacturing methamphetamine in the back of the car. Those included muriatic acid, several valves, tubing, and pseudoephedrine tablets. An officer testified that he detected a strong chemical odor coming from the car when defendant opened the door. Although a witness claimed that he placed the bucket and jars in the car without defendant's knowledge, he testified that he knew nothing about the additional items associated with manufacture that police found in the car. The jury could have inferred that defendant knew about the methamphetamine lab in her car and that she was aiding the witness in the manufacture of methamphetamine. There was evidence that defendant went to the property in a car containing an active methamphetamine lab, and from her presence on the property where people manufactured methamphetamine, the jury could have found the essential elements of manufacturing methamphetamine.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State ex rel. Pub. Disclosure Comm'n v. Permanent Offense


No. 56574-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


136 Wn. App. 277; 150 P.3d 568; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2411



November 6, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals December 20, 2006.   [***1] Order Granting Respondent's Motion to Publish filed December 20, 2006.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Permanent Offense, 135 Wn. App. 1038, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2871 (2006)
Modified by, Reconsideration denied by, Ordered published by State Ex Rel Wash. State Public Disclosure Comm'n v. Permanent Offense, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 44 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 16, 2007)
Review denied by State ex rel. Pub. Disclosure Comm'n v. Permanent Offense, 162 Wn.2d 1003, 175 P.3d 1092, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 904 (Wash., Dec. 4, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant political action committee (PAC) treasurer challenged a judgment of the Snohomish County Superior Court (Washington) that denied her motion to dismiss respondent State's action against the PAC treasurer for violations of the Washington Public Disclosure Act (PDA), Wash. Rev. Code § 42.17.010. The treasurer's motion to dismiss alleged that the PDA provisions unconstitutionally infringed on her First Amendment rights.


OVERVIEW: The State filed an action against the treasurer after an investigation into a billing scheme using a corporate entity that concealed compensation paid to another PAC worker. The treasurer filed a motion to dismiss, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court rejected the treasurer's First Amendment arguments and concluded that the disclosure provisions of the PDA that she violated, Wash. Rev. Code §§ 42.17.080, 42.17.090, and 42.17.120, as applied to her were constitutional because the State had a substantial interest in providing information to voters that was closely related to the PDA's disclosure requirements. The court noted that while the PDA's disclosure requirements did burden political speech, after-the-fact financial reporting was far less burdensome on speech than the outright prohibition by way of spending limitations. The court also rejected the treasurer's claim that the trial court lacked jurisdiction because the record established that the Public Disclosure Commission investigated the case, found "apparent" violations, and referred the case to the attorney general for prosecution in the trial court as provided in Wash. Rev. Code §§ 42.17.360 and 42.17.400.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that assessed penalties and attorney fees against the PAC treasurer and that rejected her First Amendment claims.

Barnett & Lim Assocs. v. City of Fed. Way


No. 56889-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2408



November 6, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Barnett & Lim Assocs. v. City of Fed. Way, 135 Wn. App. 1038, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2874 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord challenged an order of the trial court (Washington) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee city in the landlord's action asserting that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.46.110(4) did not allow the city to attach 3 tax liens to its property in order to collect the unpaid gambling taxes of a tenant or that, if it did allow the city to impose such a lien, the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city attached tax liens on the landlord's property based on a tenant's failure to pay gambling taxes. The landlord filed suit, and in order to sell the property, the landlord agreed to pay into the court registry proceeds from the sale equal to the amount claimed by the city under its liens. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the city. On appeal, the court vacated the trial court order. The court held that the city could not impose a lien on the landlord's property because the landlord had no beneficial interest or involvement in the underlying taxable activity. The court held that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.46.110(4) did not authorize the city to impose a lien on the landlord's property. The court noted that holding the landlord liable for the tax liability of a tenant would deprive the landlord of its property without hearing or due process of law as provided in Wash. Const. art. I, § 3 because the landlord did not owe gambling taxes and had no beneficial interest in tenant's underlying taxable activity. The court noted that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.46.270 mandated strict application of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.46.110(4) to persons permitted to engage in gambling activities.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court order granting summary judgment in favor of the city and remanded the case with directions to enter judgment for the landlord and release the registry funds to it.

State v. Scott


No. 24256-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2395



November 2, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Scott, 135 Wn. App. 1035, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2862 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 05-1-00245-3. Judge signing: ROBERT G. SWISHER. Date filed: June 10, 2005.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Superior Court County (Washington), of stalking his ex-girlfriend. Defendant appealed, contending, among other things, that the information did not include all the necessary elements of the crime, and that the evidence was insufficient to prove stalking.


OVERVIEW: Although specific reference to the victim's fear of injury was missing from the information, that element was implied by the allegation that she was intimidated, that defendant intended to frighten her, and that he knew or reasonably should have known that she was afraid. Because fear of injury was reasonably implied in the charging language, and defendant made no further argument that the inartful language prejudiced his defense, the charging document was adequate. Also, the jury was properly instructed, and defense counsel was not ineffective in failing to challenge the information, the jury instructions, or the prosecutor's cross-examination of defendant on prior crimes of dishonesty. The information and jury instructions were not defective, and the State was allowed to attack defendant's credibility on cross-examination by asking him about prior convictions involving dishonesty. Finally, defendant's frequent telephone calls and multiple incidents of following the victim, provided sufficient evidence for a rational juror to find that the victim reasonably feared defendant intended to injure her or another person.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

 

1594 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Plemmons v. Pierce County


No. 33072-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2380



October 31, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Plemmons v. Pierce County, 134 Wn. App. 449, 140 P.3d 601, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1689 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, granted summary judgment in favor of respondent arrestee on the argument that a pre-bail strip search of the arrestee, a non-violent identity-theft victim, was unconstitutional. Appellant county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that the parties agreed that the county strip-searched the arrestee as a person committed to incarceration by order of a court described in Wash. Rev. Code § 10.79.120. The county argued that its strip search was authorized under the statute. The appellate court found that Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.2 implied that a person, such as the arrestee, who was taken into custody pending posting of bail, had been ordered "released" subject to certain conditions rather than "committed to incarceration," the prerequisite for a warrantless strip search under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.79.120, not subject to the restrictions of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.79.130 and .140. The legislative history demonstrated the Legislature's intent to restrict warrantless strip searches of persons, such as the arrestee, arrested for a non-violent offense, who were to be released on bail before trial or conviction. The arrestee was in custody pending release on bail and, thus, entitled to the protections of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.79.130 through .160. These protections included a warrant, probable cause, or individualized reasonable suspicion before being strip searched, none of which was present.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment in favor of the arrestee was affirmed; the superior court's ruling that the county did not violate the statutes was vacated.

State v. Jones


No. 33828-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2393



October 31, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Jones, 135 Wn. App. 1032, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2852 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of a trial court (Washington), which convicted him of residential burglary, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.52.025(1), and four counts of first degree unlawful firearm possession, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(a). He argued, and the State conceded, that the corpus delicti rule required reversal of three of his firearm convictions. Defendant also alleged, in part, ineffective assistance of counsel and a speedy trial violation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the State violated his Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.3 right to a speedy trial, requiring dismissal of the charges with prejudice. The court disagreed, finding that regardless of whether defendant personally agreed to the continuance, as a matter of law, he waived any objection to a continuance his counsel sought on his behalf. The court next determined that by defense counsel's express decision, in a pretrial omnibus order, to forego Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.5 and 3.6 hearings, defendant waived his right to those hearings. The court rejected defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims. The court accepted the State's concession as to the corpus delicti for three of the firearm counts because although the evidence was sufficient to show that someone took the firearms and that defendant committed the residential burglary, the evidence was not sufficient, independent of defendant's incriminating statements, to infer that he was the one who took and, therefore, possessed, the firearms. The evidence was sufficient, however, to prove burglary. Finally, the court held that the trial court did not err in calculating defendant's offender score.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of residential burglary and one count of first degree unlawful possession of a firearm but it reversed his convictions for three other counts of first degree unlawful possession of a firearm and dismissed those counts with prejudice. The court remanded for resentencing.
