State v. McComb


No. 33649-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2403



October 31, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. McComb, 135 Wn. App. 1031, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2847 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from a trial court (Washington), which convicted him of second-degree assault with a deadly weapon, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.021(1)(c). He was sentenced to life in prison without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second-degree assault, domestic violence, with a deadly weapon. The trial court found that he was a persistent offender under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 9.94A, and sentenced him to life in prison without the possibility of parole. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury on third-degree assault, as defined in Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.031(1)(d). Defendant had taken a serrated kitchen knife to the bedroom where he held the serrated edge to his wife's throat, placing her in apprehension of bodily injury. No evidence pointed to defendant acting with criminal negligence rather than with intent when he held the knife to his wife's throat. Further, the trial court did not err in admitting transcripts of defendant's telephone calls to his wife. The jail recorded all inmate telephone calls out; an automated message advised the inmate that the jail would record the calls. A similar message greeted those who received the telephone calls. Thus, there was no violation of the Washington Privacy Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.73.030(1)(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1597 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Alexanderson v. Bd. of Comm'rs


No. 33750-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


135 Wn. App. 541; 144 P.3d 1219; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2285



October 17, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington superior court affirmed respondent Western Washington Growth Management Hearings Board's (Board) finding that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over appellant residents' petition to the Board opposing respondent Clark County's consent to a Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) agreement between the county and the Cowlitz Indian Tribe. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The residents argued that the trial court erred in ruling that the Board did not have subject matter jurisdiction over the MOU. The residents contended that the MOU was a de facto amendment to the county's comprehensive plan because it required the county to act inconsistently with planning policies by providing water to the subject land. The appellate court found that in the MOU, the county agreed to provide water to the subject land. In the comprehensive plan, the county agreed not to provide water at a level inconsistent with the comprehensive plan. The Tribe proposed to use the land in a manner inconsistent with the current land use designation for the subject land. The MOU superseded and amended the comprehensive plan. Because the MOU had the legal effect of amending the plan, it was a de facto amendment and the Board had jurisdiction. The MOU was not a development agreement outside the Board's jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed and remanded to the Board for further proceedings.

 

1598 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


No. 56286-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2255



October 9, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. White, 135 Wn. App. 1012, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2633 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Washington) denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained during a search of his residence and concluded that the search warrant was supported by probable cause. Defendant was found guilty in a stipulated trial of possession of methamphetamine under Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(2)(d). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the affidavit in support of the search warrant did not establish probable cause because it did not demonstrate an informant's credibility. The lack of an independent investigation of the informant's information and the absence of a history as an informant were not dispositive as other circumstances demonstrated the informant's veracity. The informant was identified by name, gave post-arrest statements against her penal interest, and provided detailed information about the drug transaction; specifically, the informant provided a detailed description of the events that took place during her visit with defendant and described seeing him go into his bedroom and return to the living room with methamphetamine, exchanging pills for the methamphetamine, and smoking some of the methamphetamine in defendant's presence. Also, despite the informant's drug addiction and criminal record, her statements were reliable. Thus, under Wash. Const. art. I, § 7 and Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(2)(d), the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress because the search warrant was supported by probable cause and in convicting him of possession of methamphetamine.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1599 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Yakima County v. Evans


No. 24199-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


135 Wn. App. 212; 143 P.3d 891; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2147



October 5, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent county commenced condemnation proceedings against appellant property owners. The Yakima County Superior Court, Washington, entered judgment in favor of the county, finding that the taking of the owners' land was for a public use and necessity. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The instant court agreed with the trial court that the taking of the land was of public use and necessity and not arbitrary and capricious. The county commissioners determined that road modifications were necessary and as minimal as feasible. The owners did not prove fraud or capricious conduct. Therefore, the instant court deferred to the county commissioners' determination of necessity. The owners' argument that they should have received personal notice of all of the public meetings leading up to the condemnation proceeding was unpersuasive. The county's legal description that did not exclude land previously acquired by it was sufficiently definite to comply with Wash. Rev. Code § 8.08.010. The trial court properly found that the county did not violate the Washington State Environmental Policy Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 43.21C, in deciding not to conduct a second environmental review. Although the owners argued that the trial court failed to comply with Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 52(c) by not providing them with notice prior to entering its findings of fact and conclusions of law, the owners failed to show that they suffered any prejudice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1600 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Collett


No. 33714-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2111



September 26, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Collett, 135 Wn. App. 1005, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2605 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to first degree burglary, first degree robbery, second degree assault, theft of a firearm, and first degree unlawful possession of a firearm. The dismissal of defendant's subsequent personal restraint petition was reversed and remanded for resentencing. Upon resentencing, the Washington trial court imposed a 75-month sentence and ordered a deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) identification analysis. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended that the provision in his sentence requiring him to submit a biological sample for DNA identification analysis was unconstitutional under Wash. Const. art. I, § 7 and that the trial court erred in concluding that his burglary and theft convictions counted as separate offenses after finding during his original sentencing that they counted as one offense under the same criminal conduct rule. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that in light of case precedent upholding Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754, defendant's constitutional challenge to § 43.43.754 failed. Because defendant's original sentence no longer existed as a final judgment on the merits, collateral estoppel did not apply; nor did the law of the case doctrine apply because the same criminal conduct issue was never before litigated. The fact that the trial court accepted defendant's invitation to reconsider its same criminal conduct determination, but did not resolve it in his favor, was not error. Even without defendant's invitation, the trial court was entitled to reconsider on remand its earlier same criminal conduct ruling on the burglary and theft counts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
